Chapter One  
About this Guide 
Intended Users 
This guide addresses all users who wish to use the Onboard Performance Tool  to 
generate takeoff performance information in a real -time environment on the flight 
deck. 
The Onboard Performance Tool  consists of  two separate applications - 
Administrator and OPT.  Administrator, which this document covers first, is used 
to set up and maintain the data used by the flight crew.  OPT , the application used 
by the crew, utilizes this data to generate the required performance information. 
No prior computer programming experience or experience with Boeing 
performance software is required to use the interface. 
What's in it 
This guide covers the following topics: 
• how to use this guide 
• where to find the web-based Administrator software 
• how to install and setup OPT, the crew software 
• what's in the software 
• how to use the software 
• how to get help 
• how to find information about a topic—appendix and glossary 
What to do next 
It is our hope that this guide is helpful to all administrators of the Onboard 
Performance Tool. If you are unfamiliar with or have not spent much time on a 
computer you might want to follow this guide for step- by-step instruction. If you 
are comfortable using Windows
® and feel like you're ready to go, follow the quick 
installation instructions Chapter 3. If at any time you encounter problems, please 
contact our office as described in Chapter 8. 

   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide

Chapter Two  
How to Use this Guide 
Conventions 
In order to help you understand the instructions provided, we have adopt ed the 
following conventions for presenting information. 
• Program names are capitalized and in italics, such as Administrator, which 
refers to the Administrator application.  This is not to be confused with the 
airline administrator, who is the person doing all of the work with 
Administrator. 
• User input operating system commands and inputs—information typed in 
by the user is indicated by Courier, 12-pt font. 
 examples: Enter Tab Shift+F1 1200.25 
• File, session, group names, locations (names and paths), text, and list 
entries—are shown in Arial, 10-pt, bold font. 
 example: 
C:\INTERFACE\SESSION.DAT 
• Buttons, list names, field names, menus, text box names, etc.—any 
interface control is indicated by Arial, 12-pt, bold font. 
 examples: File A dd to Group Ok 
• Editorial comments—shown in Times, 10-pt, bold font. 
 example: Editor's Note: An alternative to this method is to . . . 
• Example steps for you to follow are shaded, indented and preceded by an 
arrow. 
 example: 
 Access the item from the list that you want to use . . . 
• Notes, Cautions, etc.—these notes are identified by the  symbol or 
exclamation points "!!" so that they stand out; they are printed in Arial, 
12-pt, bold font with the associated text in Times, 10-pt, bold. 
 examples:  
 Note:  If you select this option before . . .   
 
!! Caution!  Be careful to . . .

Chapter Three  
How to Install and Setup the Software 
This chapter describes the computer system requirements for this software, as well as 
instructions on how to install and run a quick checkout of the Onboard Performance Tool. 
System Requirements 
In order to install and run the OPT software,  you must have a personal computer with 
Microsoft Windows  7 or later installed and operating. Refer to your Windows ® user 
documentation for further information on the system requirements for Windows®.   On the 
iPad, you must have the most recent version, or one version back, of the iPadOS operating 
system installed.  In order to use the web -based Administrator application, you must also 
have internet access, a MyBoeingFleet account, Windows 7 or later, Microsoft Internet 
Explorer
® 11 or Firefox browser, and Acrobat Reader® 10.x or more recent. 
Please refer to the appropriate application release notes for Operating System applicability.  
In addition, some combinations of font size and resolution selected via your choice of 
display driver on Windows can cause labels and text on the Onboard Performance Tool  
Windows Stand-alone dialog boxes to appear distorted or too large for the space allocated. 
OPT has the capability of adjusting these settings from within its config file, which controls 
several aspects of the display properties.  Please reference the “EFB Onboard Performance 
Tool, Initialization and Configuration File Design Description” document  for more 
information on the config file.  
Installing OPT for Windows 
The typical method for using Administrator  is through the Administrator application 
available as a web application on MyBoeingFleet  (MBF).  Access to this application will 
be through the MBF Flight Operations Performance Software page using your normal MBF 
account and password.  Access to the MBF Administrator application is discussed below. 
In ad dition to the Administrator application on MBF, one also needs to download the 
required takeoff and landing performance databases , DDG databases, secureCode2 file, 
and (for some customers) a Stab Trim and a go -around database.  These links are also 
accessed via the MBF Performance Software download page.  Th e Administrator link is 
found with the other OPT links on the MBF >> Flight Operations>> Performance Software 
download page. 
Normal Setup 
In the Windows  7® or later e nvironment, t he simplest way to setup  the Onboard 
Performance Tool is to allow the installer  program available on the MBF Performance 
Software download page  to create all necessary directories and place all of the  program 
elements and their associated files in their default locations.  Responding to prompts for 

   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 12 
directory location/name by clicking C ontinue or N ext will create the following 
directories for the purpose described.  These are the typically recommended settings for 
the Windows 7® environment.  
Directories 
C:\Users\Public\OPT 
 The executable file ( OPT.EXE) and a few files for internal  use are located in this 
directory.  
C: \Users\Public\OPT\db 
 This directory is created to store BTM & BLM (Boeing Takeoff Module & Landing 
Module) databases, BTOPS (Boeing Takeoff Performance Subroutine ) databases, 
and MLAS databases, brake cooling and non-normal databases that are needed to 
generate takeoff or landing performance information for your airplanes. If enabled, 
the BCOP (Boeing Climb Out Program) databases that generate the All Engine 
climb gradients will also be stored here.  The airline policy  (policy.sdb), airport 
(airport.sdb), and DDG databases (***.sdb) should also be stored here after they 
are created by Administrator and downloaded. The stabTrim.sdb and goAround.sdb 
files are also stored here. 
C: \Users\Public\OPT\documentation 
 This directory is created to store a complete set of the OPT  documentation, 
including this document, the databases (airport, policy and ddg)  and config file 
design documents, and release notes. 
Path definitions f or executables and internal databases will default to the directory 
specified during setup. 
Customized Setup 
If you wish, you may install the Onboard Performance Tool into a directory other than the 
default location provided.  This can be done by simply clicking on the Browse button and 
typing over the directory highlighted in the directory specification box displayed during 
the Onboard Performance Tool installation and setup. The sub-directories for the remainder 
of the software will be automatically placed as sub-directories of the location you specify. 
 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 13 
File Locations 
After the setup is complete, all files and databases for executing the software should be 
available for use as discussed above.   
 Note:  It is necessary to first develop a set of database files using Administrator and create 
an airplane definition and at least one airport before one can successfully start the 
Onboard Performance Tool software.   
 
Installing OPT for the iPad 
The iPad version of OPT may be obtained from the Apple App Store, a link to which is 
found on the iPad Home page.  Simply go to the App Store, search for “Boeing Onboard 
Performance Tool” and you’ll find the OPT application.  Follow your standard App Store 
procedure to download the application and install it.  The OPT App comes with 
demonstration data for a FLYBOEING configuration. 
 Note:  As most operators test a new version of OPT before permitting their crews to use it, 
it is important that you be aware of whether you have any airline policies 
concerning this matter and whether it is okay to download a new version of OPT.   
 
Installing OPT Windows 10 
App 
The native Windows 10 version of OPT may be obtained from the Microsoft Store.  Simply 
go to the Microsoft Store, search for “Boeing Onboard Performance Tool” and you’ll find 
the OPT Universal Windows Platform (UWP) application under Apps.  Follow your 
standard Store procedure to download the application and install it.   
The OPT UWP App can also be found using a web browser and navigating to the official 
Microsoft site.  Once in the Microsoft site, go to Store, Software & Apps, Windows apps 
and search for “Boeing Onboard Performance Tool”.  If the system requirements are met 
you will be able to download the OPT App.  
The OPT Windows 10 App comes with demonstration  data for a FLYBOEING 
configuration. 
 Note:  As most operators test a new version of OPT before permitting their crews to use it, 
it is important that you be aware of whether you have any airline policies 
concerning this matter and whether it is okay to download a new version of OPT.

Chapter Four  
How to Use Administrator 
What it's for 
The Administrator application for the Onboard Performance Tool is intended to be 
used as a data management tool to set up and maintain the data and options that the 
flight crew has access to when they use the Onboard Performance Tool on the flight 
deck.  For this purpose, the software can set up and maintain definitions of fleets of 
airplanes, whether by airframe/engine combination, or by tail number.  In addition, 
the administrator maintains the airport database, as well as the customized DDG 
database, that the Onboard Performance Tool uses to calculate takeoff performance. 
As noted previously, the Administrator application is available as a web -based 
MBF application.  T he screen pictures in this document are based on a sample 
session using this MBF application. 
Terminology 
In this section we introduce terminology that is used with this software and OPT . 
For more information on OPT, refer to the appropriate chapter. 
• Access and shortcut keys—keystroke combinations that give keyboard 
access to controls and functions 
• Controls—buttons, lists, menus, dialogs, etc. that y ou use to operate the 
interface 
• Dialog boxes—forms that appear on your screen which allow you to 
provide inputs and select functions.  Also known as windows. 
• Ellipses—the three dots ( . . .) that appear on some controls; these indicate 
that if the item is selected, additional information must be provided before 
any action is taken.  A button with only an ellipse showing indicates a 
browse function will take place upon pressing the button. 
• Functions—tasks performed by the software  
• Keyboard inputs—refers to user inputs via the keyboard 
• Mouse inputs—clicks, double-clicks, drag-drops, and moves that allow 
user input via the mouse or other pointing device 
• Navigation—moving between dialog boxes and modules to access the 
functions 
• Pages—many of the dialog boxes contain multiple pages of information. 
To access the various pages of such a dialog box, click the mouse pointer 
on the tabs that are listed on the right-hand side or top of the dialog box. 

 
OPT Administrator’s Guide

• Tabs—many of the dialog boxes contain multiple pages of information. 
The tabs that are shown are clicked to access the pages.  The tabs are 
effectively an index to the different pages.  To access a page, click on its 
tab. 
• User inputs—any  mouse or typed commands by the user

C:\Users\Public\OPT\Documentation directory.  Th e release notes may also be found 
under the OPT Support Material heading on the MBF Performance Software  >> General 
Airplane Information page. 
iPad Version 4.92 
Changes introduced in the iPad version are found in the Release Notes, which are generally 
included as part of the release announcement  and may be found under the OPT Support

page.

Changes introduced in the Windows 10 App version are found in the Release Notes, which

OPT Administrator Tool Changes to support Version 4.92

in the Release Notes, which may be found within the OPT Administrator Tool on the 
bottom left hand corner under Documentation >> Release Notes.  Once the user clicks the 
Release Notes link, they will be taken to OPT Administration Tool  Release Notes where 
the user will scroll to the bottom for the latest changes.

 Administrator Introduction 
Administrator provides extensive functionality for configuring the airborne 
application.  An airline administrator configures the module with input related to 
the airline’s dispatch policies, application behavior preferences, and display setting 
preferences.  It is important that the administrator is well- versed in commercial 
airplane performance and the governing regulations. 
Initial setup for a new airplane model is fairly extensive and can take one to two 
hours.  During this setup, the administrator imports the airplane series interface files 
(SIF) and configures a variety of application and policy settings that will rarely 
need to be changed.  After the initial setup, revising and building databases will 
only take a few minutes. 
Administrator allows users to set up and store “building blocks” for a variety of 
different operating situations.  A building block generally corresponds to a record 
set in each of the database files used by the application.  For example, an airline 
may want to use Policy Set “A” for domestic routes and Policy Set “B” for 
international routes.  Administrator allows both “A” and “B” to be configured and 
stored for later use.  One or more building blocks can be configured using 
Administrator and stored for later use.   
Instructions for creating an initial set of building blocks is described in the next 
section.  This information is stored in a SQL database used by Administrator.  The 
information the user inputs into this database via Administrator is used to create a 
set of database files  for use by OPT.  The building block data stored in the SQL 
database is the source of the database files, but is not directly linked.  Editing the 
database files outside of the module is not advised as it will introduce 
inconsistencies between the databases. 
The following examples and illustrations assume that the user is using the MBF 
version of Administrator.  In general, Administrator will appear very similar when 
run via other implementations.  The MBF version of Administrator is accessed via 
an Execute link under Performance Software → General Airplane Information → 
OPT Administrator.)

Initial Setup, Step by Step 
The following process assumes the administrator is using Administrato r to set up 
an airplane for the first time.  Before starting, the information and/or files shown in 
Table 1 below are required and should be downloaded to the administrator’s local 
PC and/or be readily available.  
Table 1 – Information and Data Required for OPT/Administrator Setup 
Information/Data Required Information/Data Source Comments 
Airplane Performance Databases (i.e. 
SCAP files for takeoff, landing and 
climbout) 
Download from the Flight 
Operations -> Performance 
Software link of the 
https://www.myboeingfleet.com/ 
site. Model Specific >> Takeoff 
and Landing Databases category 
and Climbout Databases category. 
AFM-DPI certified Airplanes: Consists 
of 8-10 individual files with a .dbn 
extension (n = 1 or 2).  Airplanes 
certified with a paper Flight Manual for 
takeoff and landing:  Consists of one or 
two files with a .bdb or .db extension.  
Some models also have a separate Non-
Normal Landing database with the .db 
extension i.e. BL3NGNNL01.db.  This 
should also be included. 
The 737NG also made available a 
separate brake cooling database to 
provide brake cooling times.  This 
database should also be included in OPT 
version 4.60 or higher to obtain brake 
cooling results.  747-400, 757s and 767s
 
also made available a separate brake 
cooling database that can be used with 
v4.90 or higher. 
For the All-Engine Climb feature, the 
climbout databases will be used and the 
following files are required (*.cnf, *dat, 
*lsp, *.opl, *.dir &.nse (future)) for each 
airframe/engine combination. 
All takeoff, landing and climbout files 
should be placed in your “OPT\dB” 
directory.   If not owned already, these 
databases may be purchased directly 
from the MBF Data & Services Catalog 
service on the MBF Home page. 
Boeing “SIF” file Download from the Flight 
Operations -> Performance 
Software link of the 
https://www.myboeingfleet.com/
 
site. Model Specific >> OPT sif 
File category 
The “SCAP Import File” contains 
information that maps the SCAP 
variables to text descriptions in the 
application.  
There are four types of SIFs 
depending on airplane type: takeoff and 
landing, takeoff only, landing only and 
climbout. 
Airplane Loadsheet – Operational CG 
limits 
Purchase from Weight Engineering 
or airline developed. 
If using the Weight and Balance 
functionality in OPT, operationally 
curtailed CG limits (i.e. CG envelope) 
are required.

 Manage Preferences 
 
Administrator unit preferences  
Administrator includes unit preference settings for both Administrator and for OPT.  Unit 
preferences set for the OPT will force the OPT application to display data in the requested 
units.  Unit preferences set for Administrator will cause the application to default to these 
units during the configuration-setup process. Administrator preferences can be overridden 
by changing unit selection on any screen in the module. The Administrator unit preferences 
simply determine the default settings of the radio buttons applicable to a set of units on the 
page.  Choose your unit preferences using the radio buttons for each of the selections.  Click 
the Save button to save your preferences  and return to the home page, while clicking on 
the Cancel button will discard any changes and return to the home page. 
 Note:  The radio button settings/units shown on any individual screen in Administrator are 
the units for the data presented on that screen, regardless of the Administrator  
preference settings.  For instance, a single airport in the airport database might 
have its runway length characteristics entered in feet by using the radio buttons on 
the runway edit screen, even though the Administrator preferences are set to meters 
for runway length.  In this case, the airport edit page settings take precedence. 
 
 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 21 
OPT unit preferences  
OPT unit preferences are accessed through the Home > App Preferences link in the left 
hand side navigation area under Preferences.  Choose your unit preferences using the radio 
buttons for each of the selections.  Click the Save  button to save your preferences  and 
return you to the home page, while clicking on the Cancel button will discard any changes 
and return you to the home page. 
 
Most of the preferences shown above are related to weight and measurement units, however, at the 
bottom of the screen, there is a section to set the display size and orientation.  In the Application 
Display Properties section (only applicable to Windows platforms), there is one line to choose the 
display size and orientation and one line to set the screen resolution.  Full Screen is an available 
option.  If the custom size is selected, the input should be made in pixels , similar to the standard 
sizes shown to the left.  For screen resolution, the custom input is made in pixels per inch and 
would typically be a number between about 90 and 130.  It is frequently necessary to use this 
custom option, as using the System Default option relies on the value reported to the Windows
® 
operating system by the monitor and experience has shown that this number is often erroneous.  If 
the fonts seem to be too large or small on your OPT installation, this is most likely the cause. The 
Application Display Properties are not applicable to the iPad application.  The iPad application is 
either full portrait or full landscape depending on the iPad settings.

OPT Folder Location – Windows® 7 
OPT is set up in such a fashion that it can opera te with all files in the same directory, or when its 
parts are split up into different directories .  For clarity purposes on your computer, it is probably 
desirable to set up your OPT installation to be in a directory by itself, with other sub-directories to 
contain some of its parts.  The default, recommended, directory structure looks like this: 
 
In addition, there are several system -level .dll files that OPT  needs to function properly.  These 
.dll files should be either in the OPT  root directory, or som ewhere checked by the Windows ® 
system path definition, such as C :\Windows\System32.  In general, it is best to leave these files 
where the OPT installer placed them. 
This folder structure is maintained using the Administrator OPT Folder Location link on the 
site map on the left side of the Administrator application.  Clicking on that link will display a 
screen that looks like that shown below. 
 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 23 
One may change any of the path names shown above to something suited to your unique needs.  
Each of the entries above are described by the following: 
• perf-scap-dir – the directory that is used to read the SCAP takeoff and landing databases.  
These are the takeoff and landing performance databases that are acquired separately and 
downloaded from MyBoeingFleet.com. 
• perf-storage-directory – the directory that is used to write the automated trace files to 
• perf-to-datastore – the file name (with path) to write the takeoff spreadsheet output to 
• perf-land-datastore – the file name (with path) to write the landing spreadsheet output to 
• perf-db-airport – the file name (with path) of the airport database 
• perf-db-policy - the file name (with path) of the policy database 
• perf-db-mmel - the file name (with path) of the DDG database 
• perf-dll-takeoff – the .dll file name (with path) of the takeoff calculation .dll 
• perf-dll-land – the .dll file name (with path) of the landing calculation .dll 
• perf-dll-ga – the .dll file name (with path) of the JAR-OPS1 go-around gradient .dll 
• perf-dll-stab – the .dll file name (with path) of the stab trim calculation .dll 
• perf-sqldll-dir – the directory that is used to store the database .dll files 
• perf-dll-fuel – the .dll file name (with path) of the customized fuel burn .dll 
• blt-document – the directory that is used to store documents for ad hoc viewing 
• blt-navdata – the directory that is used to store chart documents for ad hoc viewing 
• perf-to-vspeeds – the directory that is used to write the LDI takeoff uplink message for 
use by ground software to uplink to the airplane 
• crew-data-file – the directory that is used to store the crewdata file.ini file that contains a 
list of crew members authorized to digitally sign reports within the OPT application.  Each 
line in the file includes a crew member’s name, company ID, and an encrypted password.  
Please reference the OPT Crew Roster File Specifications (available in MBF under OPT 
Support Materials) for details on how to generate a file with password encryptions.    
 
Note that one may use either explicit Windows
® path names, or relative path names (as shown in 
the example above).  Clicking on the Reset Directory to Default Locations button will restore 
the settings to the path names described above.  Clicking on the Save button will save any changes 
that have been made and return one to the Administrator  home screen.  Clicking on the Cancel  
button will discard any changes that have been made before returning one to the Administrator  
home screen.

E-mail Preferences 
The e-Mail Preferences allow any of the applications (i.e. Stand Alone, th e iPad or 
Windows 10) to send output data (send to text option report) from the OPT Application on 
the mobile device to predefined or manually entered users’ e-mail address for analysis.  To 
activate the feature the user must check the Enable Device to Send Output Data to 
E-Mail Address box.  To predefine the e -mail addresses, click the Add button.  Enter 
one e-mail per line and multiple addresses  can also be added.   Click the Save button to 
save the e-mail preferences and return to the home page, while clicking on the Cancel  
button will discard any changes and return the user to the home page.   
 
 Note:  The e-mail Preferences is the only option that is not saved at a global company 
account level.  This preference is saved at the individual user account login.  To 
ensure the same e-mail option and addresses are available when building the OPT 
policy, please add the same e-mail address under “e-Mail Preferences” for each 
MBF login account that builds OPT data files.

Airplane Management 
 
Manage SCAP Configurations  
 
 Note:  The next several steps are all related to the navigation links under Performance 
Management  Airplane Management.  As such, Performance Management  
Airplane Management will be left off for the sake of brevity.   
 
Navigate to the screen shown using the link to Performance Management - > Airplane 
Management. This section of the module is used to import the Boeing OPT SIF (SCAP 
Import File).  The Boeing OPT SIF is a text file that provides a complete description of the 
SCAP parameters applicable to a given SCAP database for takeoff and landing.  There is 
also an All-Engine SIF that provides a description of the corresponding Climbout Database 
that should be used when creating the policy definition.   The performance databases for 
takeoff, landing and climbout (if used) must be present either in the db directory or 
perf_perf part for the iPad application to run the data.        
 
 
a. Click on the Manage SCAP Configurations link to import a new SIF file 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide

b. Click on the button for the file type you want to import: Takeoff SCAP, 
Landing SCAP or Climbout Config in the upper screen 
c. Click on the Import button at the bottom – you will be prompted to browse for a 
Boeing SIF file on your local computer or network drive.  
d. Click the Choose File button to navigate to the desired SIF file, select the SIF 
(click Open), and click Continue. 
e. The next figure shows the resulting screen if a SIF for an AFM-DPI model was 
imported, where you will be prompted to enter a Configuration Title for takeoff 
calculations and landing calculations.  In this example, the title 787-8_Trent-AE-
Tko was used to identify the takeoff configuration and the title 787-8_Trent-AE-
LDG was used to identify the landing configuration. 
 
 Note:  Some older Boeing SIF files are good for both BPS and OPT application.  The 
latest versions of OPT SIFs are found in the “OPT sif Files” category in 
Performance Software under the specific model.   A SIF with product 
description that starts as follows OPT_sif_file_C**** is for the Climbout 
Configuration (All Engine) while any other SIFs are for takeoff or landing.  The 
corresponding SCAP database name is found in the product description of the 
SIF file for any type of database.   
 
 
f. Click the Import button to assign the newly created titles to the SIF 
configuration.  This will return you to the Takeoff SCAP Configurations summary 
page shown below. 
g. In the “Manage Takeoff SCAP Configuration” screen and in the “Manage 
Landing SCAP Configuration” screen, confirm that your SIF has been imported 


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide

Page 30 
and the titles have been assigned. Your SCAP configuration setup is now 
complete.  
h. To view the configurations available for takeoff, click on the Takeoff SCAP 
button.  It is important to pay attention to the ACMDBI referenced and the 
revision number.  These fields MUST match the AFM-DPI database being used. 
i. To view the configurations available for landing, click on the Landing SCAP 
button.  For those databases that have a separate Non-Normal database, it is 
important to pay attention to the Revision referenced.  The revision must match 
the version of the Non-Normal Landing (NNL) database being used.  For 
example, if the Revision is “S003-A/1.3.0”, S003 is the revision of the AFM-DPI 
database and 1.3.0 is the version of the NNL database expected by OPT.

button.

configuration. The Update option allows the user to keep previously created 
configurations.  When this needs to be done, click the Update button, use the 
browse button to select the new .sif file, and then click Continue to import the 
new file and update your setup.

The OPT sif files that have the PRODUCT name in MyBoeingFleet that start with

databases require the following files (*.cnf, *.dat, *.lsp, *.opl, *.dir & *.nse) for each 
airframe/engine combination.  The steps described below tell OPT what databases to use 
for the calculations.

upper screen 
c. Click the Import button at the bottom of the screen – you will be prompted to 
browse for a Boeing Climbout SIF on your local computer or network drive.

Continue.

Manage Takeoff Runway Conditions/Crosswinds  
Once your SCAP configuration setup is complete, you can assign policy and 
configuration options to that Configuration.  
a. From the Airplane Management Screen, click on the Manage Policy & Config 
Options link on the Airplane Management screen and then select the Manage 
Runway Takeoff Conditions/Crosswinds  link.  This screen, shown below, 
allows you to input the maximum allowable crosswind for each runway condition 
available in each SIF stored in Administrator .  Select  the desired Takeoff 
configuration from the drop down menu first to assign any input winds to that 
configuration.  If other SIFs were stored in Administrator (e.g. for a different 
airplane model), max crosswind values can (and must) be stored and assigned for 
each SIF.  This page also allows the user to input minimum and maximum values 
for contaminant depth.  The values may not be less than or greater than the 
minimum or maximum respective values as noted in the SCAP database release 
notes. 
 Note:  The crosswind values entered into Administrator are not AFM limitations and 
will not inhibit the flight deck user from running takeoff/landing calculations 
with inputs that exceed the module values.  They will simply trigger a 
warning message to check crosswind values.   
 
b. Note that each Condition Name can be changed on the first column as desired.  
The user can rename any runway condition.  For example, DRY can be renamed 
as 6-DRY if applicable to your operations. 
 
c. Note that the radio buttons for “Wind Unit” default to the units set in the 
Administrator Preferences (“Knots” in this example) 
 
d. Note that you can change the “Depth Unit” to either mm or in.  The Min and Max 
Depth will be based on the selected units.  The OPT application will default to 
the selected depth units but the end user can change the entry unit if desired via 
the application when entering the runway condition depth.  The min depth and 
max depth can be edited as desired.  This will be the values enforced by the 
application.  Ensure that the Min and Max values entered for contaminant depth 
are supported by the takeoff performance database.  
 
e. Factor Depth and Copy/Del can be used together.  Factor Depth has been 
supported by the application since OPT version 4.80. The Copy/Del allows the 
user to copy an existing runway condition.  The Administrator Tool will now 
allow the ability to specify the factor to correlate an existing database runway 
condition to a desired runway condition not supported by the takeoff performance 
database.  As an example, “Wet Snow” is not supported for the 737NG (600/-
700/-800-900), if the user would like to add “Wet Snow” to the list of selectable 
runway conditions in OPT, the user would perform the following steps:  

   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 34 
 
1. Click on the copy icon for the “Slush” runway condition  
2. Rename the “Condition Name” from “SLUSH-COPY” to “Wet 
Snow”. 
3. Readjust the Min and Max Depth accordingly. 
4. Type “2” under Factor Depth.  This is the Boeing recommended 
correlation for Wet Snow for 737 NG airplanes.  The Administrator 
can reference the latest Boeing Guidance by reviewing the “Global 
Reporting Format and Correlation with Existing Boeing Airplane 
Databases” presentation from the “2022 Boeing Performance and 
Flight Operations Engineering Conference”.

Slippery Runway Conditions  
Slippery runway conditions are defined by your airline and generally conform to industry 
standards or data that has been provided by the airframe manufacturer.  Boeing has 
historically published slippery runway data as a function of airplane braking “mu” (i.e. 
Greek letter, µ), which is a measure of the airplane braking effectiveness on a particular 
runway surface.  This should not be confused with “ surface friction µ”, which may be 
available from ground friction measuring vehicles.  Typical values of slippery runway 
braking 
µ are shown in Table 2. 
 
Table 2 – Typical Airplane Braking Mus 
 
Airplane Braking 
(Slippery) µ 
Typically Reported As Comment 
0.200 Good 
Approximates the braking 
action typical of a wet 
runway.  


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 36 
0.150 Good to Medium  
0.100 Medium Also reported as “Average” 
0.075 Medium to Poor  
0.050 Poor 
Approximates the braking 
action on wet ice.  Virtually 
“nil” braking 
Note that slippery runway conditions are established by airline or regulatory policy and are 
not dependent on airframe type.  An airline may decide to define an airplane braking µ of 
0.15 as “medium” for model type “A,” because they feel that model A, or the airports it 
serves, warrant less conservatism.  Model type “B” might define “medium” using a braking 
µ of 0.10.  The module allows the administrator to provide definitions of each slippery 
condition type defined by the airline.  Note that the slippery runway conditions must be 
defined for each menu they are to be used from, e.g. the takeoff, landing dispatch, and 
landing enroute menus.  If a slippery condition contains the word WET in the condition 
name the OPT application will allow assumed temperature for this runway condition 
regardless of the mu (
µ) value. 
 Note:  The administrator sets up all possible runway conditions for the airline fleet on this 
screen, but actual selection of which conditions apply to a particular airplane comes 
later in Step 6 of 10: Takeoff Layout - View/Define options for selected 
buttons. of Create Policy Definition during the process of creating the data files. 
Manage Dispatch Landing Runway Conditions/Crosswinds  
Manage Enroute Landing Runway Conditions/Crosswinds  
Administrator allows the user to set up completely separate sets of allowable runway 
conditions and crosswinds for both the dispatch landing and enroute landing cases in a 
manner identical to that discussed for the takeoff conditions.  In addition, the user may 
specify, for both landing cases, a user-defined flare distance, field length increment, and 
factor that may be applied specifically for each runway condition.  This is to allow for 
compliance with local regulations that may require certain minimum distances and 
factors when computing landing distance requirements for the enroute case.  They are not 
typically required for the dispatch case.  However, a 15% landing distance factor may 
also be applied to non-dry, non-wet dispatch runway conditions depending on the 
regulatory bases of the performance database.  A typical input screen is shown below. 
 
If the input flare distance is left at zero, the flare distance that OPT uses will be the flare 
distance calculated using the SCAP landing performance database.  The total calculated 
distance for landing is equal to (((flare + stopping distance) + Land Increment) * Land 
Factor).  Note that not all SCAP databases allow the input of a user-defined flare 
distance.  For those databases that do not allow the user-defined flare distance, the user 
can use the Land Increment (i.e. 500 ft) to simulate an equivalent flare distance of 1500 

 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 37 
feet.  To check if the database supports the Flare Distance input see the SCAP database 
user guide for parameters: RWYDL(7) & RWYDL(8). 
 
 
 Note:  Because the enroute landing distance regulatory guidance has been changing over 
the last several years, users should refer to current regulatory guidance material, as 
well as guidance information produced by Boeing Flight Operations Engineering 
when setting up their enroute landing settings.   
                             Boeing has published document D6-86047, “Advisory Method for Computing 
TALPA ARC Consistent Data”, that can be found under Flight Operations >> 
Performance Manuals >> General Performance Information >> TALPA-ARC to 
help establish enroute landing settings for OPT.   
Manage Non-Normal Max Crosswinds and Alerts  
Administrator introduced the ability to setup crosswinds for each non-normal landing 
(NNL) scenario during landing enroute calculations in support of OPT v4.80. Another 
enhancement was made in v4.90, enabling the customization of a Message for each non-
normal situation. This message will be displayed to the flight crew after they click on the 
Calculate button for the desired NNL.  For example, the 777 HYD PRESS SYS R+C 
QRH has the following: “Crosswind limit for landing is 20 knots.”   The Manage Non-
Normal Max Crosswinds screen enables users to enter maximum crosswind values for 
any of the non-normals.  If these crosswind values are left blank, the application will 
default to using the landing enroute runway condition crosswind limits.  However, if the 
Max Crosswind value is specified for a Non-Normal, OPT will use that value unless the 
runway condition limit is lower.  To set this up, from the Airplane Management Screen, 
click on the Manage Policy & Config Options link on the Airplane Management 
screen and then select the Manage Non-Normal Max Crosswinds link.  This screen, 
shown below, allows you to input the maximum allowable crosswind for each non-


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 38 
normal condition.  These NNL conditions were imported during the OPT SIF import 
process and are now stored in Administrator.  First, select the desired Aircraft Type 
from the drop down menu and then select the Aircraft Config.  
If you would like to display an ALERT MESSAGE to the flight crew for any NNL, you 
can enter the desired message for each specific NNL under NNC Alert Messages.  
Please note that the OPT application will only allow a maximum of 255 characters for 
this message.

Manage Lineup Allowance 
Depending on your local regulations, the use of lineup allowances may be required.  The 
figure below shows the input screen for setting up lineup allowances. These allowances are 
subtracted from the accelerate- stop (ASDA) and accelerate- go (TODA) distances when 
calculating field -limit performance.  When the page is first selected, the Stop and Go 
distance values are blank.   
a. Select the Aircraft Type using the drop down menu near the top of the page.  
This menu is populated by the aircraft types available on the SIF import screen 
after completing Step 2 (click on Performance Management - > Airplane 
Management -> Manage SCAP Configuration to view the aircraft types you 
have entered). 
b. Values for 90° and 180° taxiway entrances are required.  Enter your own 
preferred values, or click Default to have these values populated by the Boeing 
default values for the selected aircraft type, as published in the FAA “Takeoff 
Safety Training Aid”, Appendix 4-I . 
c. Note: the default units come from the administrator unit preference settings. If 
your data is not in the desired units, select the appropriate radio button for your 
unit settings.  The radio button setting will override settings in the administrator 
preferences and be applied to all data on the screen. 
d. Click Add to add new values (e.g. for different taxiway entrances). 
e. Click Save to save changes and return to the previous screen.  Click Cancel  
to discard changes and return to the previous screen.

Manage Weight and Balance  
The Weight and Balance module i n OPT is set up entirely within the Administrator  
application.  The user should have the airplane’s Weight and Balance manual available and 
all pertinent weighing data for each airplane to be  set up.  It is also necessary to have the 
allowable c.g. envelope which has been curtailed for in -flight movement of items such as 
gear, flaps, fuel, passengers, etc. 
 
 Note:  Unless using the Active Curtailments feature (described in the Create 
Policy Definitions section later), it is important that one does NOT use the 
AFM certified c.g. envelope for checking c.g. limits within OPT.  The c.g. 
envelope data input in Administrator for this purpose should be curtailed 
for in-flight movement of gear, flaps, fuel, passengers, etc. 
 
The W&B module starting with OPT version 4.30 provides the ability to divide the weight 
entries into 5 different types : setup, passengers , cargo, last minute changes corrections  
and/or fixed items , and fuel.   When first entering the OPT  W&B screen, you would 
normally see a window that appears something like that shown below. 
 
In this example, the green highlighted SETUP button shows that the setup window is being 
displayed.  On this setup window, the administrator has a weight starting p oint defined of 
BW (basic weight), flight crew selections defined, cabin crew selections defined,  catering 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide

Page 41 
selections defined, and potable water selections defined.  Each question mark “?” has help 
information defined by the administrator in the Administrator.  In the center of the screen, 
the current structural weights are shown in larger, bold typeface, with the maximum 
allowed values shown in parentheses.  At the bottom of the screen, the curtailed envelope 
is shown.  As the weight inputs are updated by  the crew, a line representing the weight 
build-up for the flight is shown. 
The W&B module in OPT defined using the “ No” option for “Activate Advance Empty 
Weight option? (OPT v4.3 & greater)” in “Step 8 of 10: Allow Weight and Balance?” of a 
Build ID unde r “Create Policy Def” appears something like this when entering the OPT  
W&B screen. 
 
 
In the above example, the W&B section is divided into four (4) different types: passengers, 
cargo, last minute changes corrections (“other”) and fuel.  T he green highlighted PAX 
button shows that the passenger window is being displayed.  On this passenger window, 
the administrator has set up 7 different passenger zones.  In each case, the passenger zone 
name is listed and the maximum number of passengers is displayed in parentheses.   
The airline administrator uses the W&B functions in Administrator  to create the input 
screens for OPT  and customize it to their operational needs.  This requires detailed 
knowledge of the airline’s Weight and Balance system, zones, passenger weights, and 
curtailed envelope characteristics.

Adding Passenger Types 
In order to add passenger types,  e.g. adult, male, female, child, infant, to the Weight and 
Balance (W&B) definition, one simply selects “Manage Passenger Type” from the Manage 
Weight & Balance Settings dropdown list .  The first time one does this, a blank list for 
passenger type appears, just like with the passenger zone list.  Clicking on the Add button 
in the passenger type list will display a new, blank entry line as shown below. 
 
Passenger Type Title is the title that will be displayed in OPT  if more than one type of 
passenger is se lected; Description is a short text descriptor for reference purposes only ; 
Weight Per PAX is the weight assigned per passenger type ; Min Weight Per Pax is the 
minimum weight allowed for this passenger type ; Max Weight Per Pax is the maximum 
weight allowed for this passenger type.   Min and Max weight per pax types are enforced 
by OPT if the a dministrator elects to allow the end user to manually enter a weight 
allowance (i.e. 99.5 kg) in OPT to be used instead of using the predefined weight per pax.  
For example, some might elect to call the fifth passenger type duffels/pet  or Actual and 
elect to make this a weight that is manually entered by the flight crew. Or others might 
carry sports team and need to enter the Actual weight  for better weight tracking .  T he 
selection of whether or not to make the passenger type editable is done in Step 8b of 10: 
Define Airplane Passenger Zones for your aircraft type of Create Policy Definition.     
Once you have completed entering the information, click on Save to save the changes. 
 
Adding Cargo Zones 
In order to add cargo zones to the Weight and Balance (W&B) definition, one simply 
selects Manage Cargo Zone from the Manage Weight & Balance Settings dropdown list .  
The first time one does this, a blank list for cargo zones appears, just like with the passenger 
zone list.  Clicking on the Add button in the cargo zone list will display a new, blank entry 
line as shown below.

in the OPT Cargo tab.  The weight of bags will be subtracted from the max cargo weight

the “Wt Per Bag” and the total weight of bags will be displayed under WT of BAGS.  The 
CARGO weight can be entered for each zone.  Total WT includes both the weight of bags

Adding Cargo Positions 
OPT has the capability to manage cargo positions within the cargo zones that were just set 
up in the section above.  Note that at this time BAGS are not supported for Cargo Positions.    
To add cargo positions , one selects Manage Cargo Position from the Manage Weight & 
Balance Settings dropdown list .  Then one selects the Cargo Zone from the “Available 
Cargo Zones:” dropdown list that one wishes to manage positions for.  When that is done, 
clicking on the Add button will display a blank input form for adding cargo positions to 
the cargo zone that has been selected.  This is shown below.  Cargo positi ons may be set 
up in left/right pairs, or by a single center position.  To input a single center position, one 
must first check the Single Position check box on the left side of the input form.  Note that 
OPT does not balance for lateral loads – only longitudinally.  The user can choose up to 
fourteen (14) cargo position for each zone per tail.  A maximum of 14 cargo positions are 
allowed for OPT v4.80 and higher while a m aximum of only 5 cargo positions were 
allowed prior to OPT v4.80.

Adding Fixed Weight Allowances 
Fixed weight allowances, which  can be used for  tracking items such  as spares kits or 
different galley configurations are handled by displaying a check box in OPT for each item 
entered.  By choosing Manage Fixed Zone in the Manage Weight & Bal ance Settings 
dropdown list, the list of fixed weight items that have been entered are displayed for the 
currently selected model.  Just like the passenger and cargo lists, this list initially is empty, 
but by clicking on the Add button, the following is displayed. 
 
Fixed Weight Item Title is the title that will be displayed in OPT for this item; Description 
is a short text descriptor for reference purposes only; Weight of Item is the weight for this 
item; Balance Arm is the item’s balance arm, set in the units specified by the balance arm 
units radio buttons. 
Once you have completed entering the information, click on Save to save the changes. 
Managing Fuel Tanks 
OPT has the capability to handle several different fuel tanks, including wing tanks, center 
tanks, and multiple auxiliary tanks or tank groups.  Each of these tanks, or groups may be 
addressed using a variable balance arm that is entered as a function of tank capacity, or a 
constant value for the entire tank load.  Typically, OPT will assume that the fuel tanks use 
fuel serially; that is, the fuel is assumed to be burned from all of the auxiliary fuel tanks 
first, from the last auxiliary fuel tank entered, to the first.  Then the fuel is burned from the 
center before burning any fuel from the wing tanks.  Fuel usage schemes any more 
complicated than this may be dealt with by contacting Boeing for a customized fuel usage 
utility.  Once again, clicking on the Add button will display the blank fuel tank entry form 
shown below.

text descriptor for reference purposes only; Tank Type  is a drop down list displaying the 
choices Wing Tank, Center Tank, and Auxiliary; Tank Capacity is the entry for the 
maximum tank volume in the units selected above the tank list box; Balance Arm is the 
item’s balance arm, set in the units specified by the balance arm units radio buttons.  Please 
save the newly created fuel tank data before editing the balance arm information by clicking 
on the Save button.

Managing C.G. Envelopes 
To view the list of c.g. envelopes, one chooses Manage CG Envelope from the Manage 
Weight & Balance Settings drop list. 
 
 Note:  It is important that one does NOT use the AFM certified c.g. envelope for checking  
c.g. limits within OPT.  The c.g. envelope data input in Administrator for this 
purpose should be curtailed for in-flight movement of gear, flaps, fuel, passengers, 
etc. 
 
 Note:  OPT has the capability to continuously monitor the forward and aft c.g. limits for 
each envelope as the weight of the airplane is changed.  This means, however, that it 
is important that the c.g. envelope that is input must be single continuous function, 
meaning that for each weight input (the y axis value) there is only one forward and 
one aft c.g. value possible (x axis).   
Clicking on the Add button when the Manage CG Envelope list box is displayed will show 
a new blank entry line as shown below. 
 
 
 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 49 
CG Envelope Name is the name of the c.g. envelope that is used mainly for record keeping 
purposes, as is the information entered in the description box.  The CG Envelope Type 
drop list allows the users to specify whether the specific c.g. envelope is a takeoff, landing, 
or zero fuel weight envelope.  Define as many envelopes required for your specific aircraft.  
The user can define multiple takeoff envelopes i.e. a normal load, a tail fuel load, an 
Alternate CG en velope, and/or an alternate takeoff weight .  When Creating the Policy 
Definition, the user can specify which envelope to use and for what instance.  The user also 
has the ability to create rules that tell OPT under which circumstances  to use the selected 
envelope.  For example, if tail fuel is loaded then use the tail fuel envelope or if a MLW is 
greater than X then switch the ZFW envelope. 
Clicking the Edit…  button will display the following window. 
 
The graphic above already has some points in it to illustrate other features.  Entries are 
made into the table in the list box by inputting a weight and c.g. position into the e ntry 
boxes on the left and then clicking the Add button or the Enter key.  This action will move 
the weight and c.g. into the list on the right  and will also update the plot on the right side 
of the screen.  If the entry did not end up in the portion of the list that it should be, select 
the line by clicking on it then use the up and down arrows on the right to move it to the 
desired location.  Please pay special attention to the note above which points out the 
requirement for the c.g. envelope to be a sing le, continuous function and also all values 
(weight & cg) should be entered clockwise starting with the lowest fwd cg and increasing 
to the aft limit.  Failure to observe these  limitations will result in a n OPT program error 
and failure to function properly.   
Selecting one of the lines in the list on the right and clicking on the Delete button will 
delete that weight and c.g. position from the database.

accounting for different number of passengers onboard (i.e. define potable water vs.

selections in OPT  for “Potable Water”.  In order to add Potable Water  by Pax  Count 
scenarios to the Weight and Balance (W&B) definition, the user selects Potable Water 
Load by Pax Count in the Manage Weight & Balance Settings dropdown list.   The first 
time one does this, a blank list appears and by clicking the Add button a new entry can be 
added. 
 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide

The Potable Water Load by Pax Count Title  is the name that will be displayed in the 
dropdown selections in OPT for “Potable Water”; Help Text is a short help descriptor used 
to clearly define options being selected by the user in OPT when clicking “?” next to this 
selection; Define Potable Water Load by Pax Count is the entry to manage the potable 
water weight vs. passenger count relationship. The weight and balance arm units  for the 
definitions entered are set by the units specified in the radio buttons in this screen.  Please

be able to enter the number of passengers, weight and balance arm relationships. 
 
The first time one does this, a blank list appears and by clicking the Add button a new 
entry can be added. 
Number of Passengers  is the number of passengers required for a specific amount of 
potable water; Weight  is the weight for this specific item; Balance  Arm is the item’s 
balance arm. Add different passenger counts to fill the table.  If this option is selected in 
the application, OPT will programmatically add the water weight to the ZFW based on the 
number of passengers entered for a particular flight.   
Selecting one of the lines in the list on the right and clicking on the Delete button will 
delete from the database. 
Once you have completed entering the information, click on Save to save the changes. 
Adding Flex Weights 
Flex Weights which are optionally defined and labeled in the Administrator will be used 
to define alternate certificate limitations to operate the airplanes at alternate Maximum 
Taxi (Max Taxi), Maximum Takeoff (Max TOW), Maximum Zero Fuel (Max ZFW), and 
Maximum Landing (Max LW) weights in lieu of the 


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 56 
MTW/MTOW/MZFW/MLW found in the base AFM. The original certified limits as well 
as the alternate weights can be selected from the OPT Setup page for a given flight. The 
flex weight definitions are handled by displaying a drop down list in OPT next to the 
“Start With” button.  The original certified weights must also be added in the Flex 
Weight list below for selection by the user.  The flex weight selected becomes the new 
limits for the takeoff and landing calculations in OPT.  In order to add Flex Weight 
scenarios to the Weight and Balance (W&B) definition, the user selects Manage Flex 
Weight in the Manage Weight & Balance Settings dropdown list.   The first time one 
does this, a blank list for Manage Flex Weight appears, by clicking on the Add button a 
new entry can be added. 
 
The Flex Weight Title is the name that will be displayed in the dropdown selections in 
OPT for “Flex Wt”; Boeing recommends that this title be kept to six characters (i.e. the 
takeoff weight) so that it will fit on the screen.  The administrator should use the Help Text 
which is a help descriptor to clearly define options being selected by the user in OPT when 
clicking “?” next to this selection.  Max Taxi, Max TOW, Max ZFW, and Max LW are 
the weights specific to the Flex Weight being defined.  
Once you have completed entering the information, click on Save to save the changes. 
 
 Note:   The Weight Unit in the Manage Flex Weight  section must match the weight units 
under the Weights section of Step 3 of 10: Set Airplane operational weights, takeoff 
and landing settings.

Manage Takeoff Policy  
The Manage Takeoff Policy  link on the Manage Policy  and Configuration Options 
screen will display the screen shown below. 
 
Selecting a takeoff configuration from the pull -down menu will then display the lists of 
available SCAP settings for each variable that can be set by the Administrator.  This list 
represents the baseline, or default setting, for each of those variables.  The baseline setting 
is the setting which is used if there is no button created for modifying the setting when 
using OPT.  As an example, an airline might want to enforce a one -flap takeoff policy.  
This can be done by selecting the flap selection radio button for the desired flap and 
removing the flap button from the standard user interface.  A typical screen with this 
information is shown below.  Note the scroll bar that is circled on  the right side.  It is 
important to recognize that there may be some settings hidden below the original view.  
One should scroll down to see the entire list of items available for selection to verify proper 
settings. 
 
  
Once you have made the desired selections, clicking on Save  will save the settings.  
Clicking on Cancel  will return the user to the previous screen and discard any changes 
that were made.

Page 58 
787 Fuel Jettison Return-to-Land, 737 MAX, and 777-9 
When complying with FAR 1001, the 787, 737 MAX, and 777-9 are required to further 
restrict the performance limited takeoff weight based on specific requirements associated 
with a return-to-land scenario.  To assist with this compliance, the Manage Takeoff Policy 
page above has landing configuration default settings to set for this scenario.  The items to 
set include a pproach air conditioning (if supported by the model), approach anti -ice, 
approach and landing flap position, and whether or not to account for inflight icing.  T he 
inflight icing penalty associated with the 787-9 has been removed from the AFM.  Please 
ensure that the Approach Flap selected is a valid combination with the landing flap position 
selected.

screen will display the Manage Landing Policy screen.  This policy screen serves the same 
purpose and is handled in a manner identical to the Manage Takeoff Policy screen 
described in the previous section.

Create Policy Definition  
Creating the final policy definition and user interface layout is the final step in the Airplane 
management activity.  From the Airplane Management screen, clicking on the Create 
Policy Definition link will display the screen shown below.   
 
Clicking on an existing Build ID will activate the buttons at the bottom of the screen.  When 
an existing Build ID is selected, clicking on the Print Summary  button w ill send a 
summary of that build to a Windows ® printer or create a PDF file with all the selections 
for that Build ID.  Clicking on the Edit Build button will enter the editing process which 
is identical to the creation process described next.  Clicking on the Remove Build button 
will allow the user to remove/delete that Build ID from the database.  Clicking on the Copy 
Build button will allow the user to copy and rename the build.  This is useful when creating 
a build for a similar tail that might only have weight changes or some other minor change.  
Clicking on the Rename Build button will allow the user to rename the selected Build ID.  
Otherwise, clicking on the < - Create Build ID -> list item will activate the Create Build 
button.  When the Create Build  button is clicked, the user enters a step- by-step process 
to create the final product.  This is the same process  that is used to edit an existing Build 
ID.  Initially, the following screen is displayed, showing Step 1 of this process.  Note that, 
depending on the options one chooses during this process, some of the screens  shown 
below may be skipped. 


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide

Page 60 
 
 
 
At this poi nt, the user enters a name for the Build ID and selects an aircraft type.  The 
aircraft type list contains a listing of the different models for which there has been data 
entered in previous steps that have already been discussed.  In this example, we have used 
a Build ID of “ N7878” and selected the 7 87-8 model from the Aircraft Type pull -down 
list.  Once both of those items have been done, the Next Step-> button is activated for use 
and clicking on it will display the next screen.  Each time a Next Step -> button is clicked 
on during this creation/edit process, the changes that have been made are saved.  Clicking 
on the Exit Steps  button on each page will return one to the Create Policy Definition 
starting point.  The next screen in the process is shown below.

Page 63 
The entry fields for this page deal with aircraft weight  information and various policy  
settings.  The Comments field at the top of the page is used for entering comments that 
describe this Build ID and only appear here.  In the Weights section, most of the entries 
are self-explanatory, but it is important to note that the Maximum Takeoff  (MTOW) and 
Maximum Landing (MLW) weights are used to define the structural  limit weights for 
takeoff and landing weight calculations, in addition to the limit weights shown on the OPT 
W&B screen.  The other entries in this section are optional unless using the W&B 
capability.  If using W&B, then all items in this section are mandatory.   In addition, the 
Maximum Zero Fuel Wt ( MZFW) entry is mandatory for the 787, 737 MAX and 777- 9 
because the fuel jettison return -to-land (RTL) scenario requires a MZFW entry.   For the 
airplanes that have RTL, the default is to have the Include ZFW entry box on takeoff 
page checked.  If you elect to remove the ZFW entry box in OPT  by unchecking the 
Include ZFW entry box on takeoff page checkbox, OPT will always use the MZFW 
entered in this step to perform the takeoff calculations.  Some users expressed the desire to 
also display the ZFW box in OPT takeoff dispatch as a m eans to have the flight crew be 
aware that there are two different weights : TOW and ZFW to avoid confusion when they 
are entering the weights in OPT from a different source.  If the desire is to also display the 
ZFW box in OPT  for those airplanes that do not have the RTL option, then check the 
checkbox for Include ZFW entry box on takeoff page (no impact to takeoff 
calcs).   If this box is left unchecked , OPT will only display the TOW entry box on 
Takeoff-Dispatch.   
 
 Note:  It is important to recognize that for those aircraft (i.e. 737-200/-300-/400/-
500/-600/-700/-800/-900, 747s, 757s, 767s, and 777s) that do not include the RTL 
scenario in the takeoff performance calculation, if the ZFW entry box is displayed, 
the ZFW entered does not have any impact on the takeoff performance calculations. 
 
In the Takeoff Settings section, there are entries to manage the engine -out acceleration 
altitude and improved climb policies, in addition to several additional takeoff policies.  For 
the level-off height policy, the administrator, enters the minimum desired level-off height.  
The lowest acceptable value here is 400 feet (per the Airplane Flight Manual) , but it is 
common to enter values of 800 feet or higher.  When doing the takeoff calculation, OPT  
will display this height, or the minimum height required to legally clear any obstacles, 
whichever is higher.  Under this entry box are a few selections which need to be  made to 
further define this height.  First, of course, are the units associated with this  entry.  The 
next selections determine whether this number is input as pressure altitude or geometric 
height and whether or not to display this number in OPT as pressure altitude or geometric 
height.  Lastly, one chooses between displaying the level -off altitude as AGL (above 
ground level) or MSL (mean sea level) altitudes/heights.  Traditional paper takeoff analyses 
were somewhat limited in that they would only display AGL geometric heights, requiring 
the crew to do some work to get the level-off height into a form which could be easily and 
properly used.  On the other hand, OPT  can display level-off height in terms of pressure 
altitude and MSL directly, which is the way most crews operate the airplane.  Note that if 

   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 64 
one chooses to report as Pressure Altitude and reference it to MSL, OPT  will report the 
baro-corrected acceleration altitude, which is equal to the sum of the airport elevation plus 
the pressure altitude AGL of the level-off height. 
When the Climbout configuration is activated in either the Administrator  or EFB OPT 
Admin site (the OPT “CAM”) or when doing administration for the 787 on the EFB OPT 
Admin site (the OPT “CAM”), there are two more fields in this area that need entries.  For 
the 787 these entries MUST be defined in order for the takeoff uplink message to be sent 
correctly.  We recommend that you use the values that match your Takeoff Ref Page from 
the FMC.  These same values will pre-populate the Takeoff All-Engine page parameters if 
the Climbout configuration is activated: 
 
The first of these fields, All-Engine Acceleration Altitude, is simply that, the altitude that 
you would normally have the FMC all -engine acceleration altitude programmed to.  The 
second field, the FMC Thrust Reduction (Alt/Flap) may be entered as either an altitude in 
a manner to the two preceding altitudes, or as a flap position.  If one elects to enter a flap 
position, one must  specify a flap position that is less than the s mallest allowed takeoff 
flap position or the FMC will reject the takeoff uplink message.  For the 787, that means 
that the only allowable entry for flap position in this field would be 1, as there is a flaps 5 
takeoff flap position. 
Some users would like t o change the outputs label shown by OPT.  The user can change 
the output label shown in OPT by entering them in the highlighted boxes below.   
 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 65 
Selections are also made for: 
• Select Optimum Flaps for Max. Assumed Temp. 
o This option will instruct OPT  to look for the absolute best assumed 
temperature by checking all  available flap positions.  If unchecked, OPT  
will use for its assumed temperature calculation the flap position that yields 
the best takeoff weight from the runway for the prevailing conditions.  I f 
checked, OPT will check all flaps, and the calculation may increase 
dramatically. 
• If a 737 airplane is being defined there are two additional takeoff options 
o Use R-label on assumed temp power setting  
o Use D- label on assumed temp power setting 
• This option is only for the power setting label on the 737 OPT  
takeoff output area, so that it will match the FMC label used for 
power setting.  It does not affect OPT calculations.   R stands for 
reduced and D stands for derate. Choose the appropriate option for 
your aircraft. 
• Select Best Derate for All Available Ratings 
o This option will cause OPT to display an OPTIMUM selection on the thrust 
rating button.  When the user selects this option, OPT will solve for the best 
combination of assumed temperature and the lowest derated thrust level (i.e. 
TO-2) for the input or planned weight.  This was the default behavior prior 
to OPT version 4.80.  In OPT version 4.80, the application defaulted to 
providing the lowest power setting.  A new check box (Use the lowest power 
setting instead of the lowest derated thrust level ) is introduced to allow 
airlines to select which method they would like to use. 
o OPT will also solve for rating that provides highest gross weight when 
solving for maximum takeoff weight.   
• Use the lowest power setting instead of the lowest derated thrust level 
o When the user selects this option, OPT will solve for the best combination 
of assumed temperature and fixed derate that provides the most thrust 
reduction (lowest power setting) for the input or planned weight.  
o OPT will also solve for rating that provides highest gross weight when 
solving for maximum takeoff weight.   
• ATM default value (leave blank if MAX) 
o  Entering a value in this box will cause OPT  to use it as the default value 
for the ATM button in t he Takeoff Dispatch page.  The value here will be 
passed to each calculation regardless of whether the ATM button is shown.  
For example, some airlines use a - 2 degree buffer  to the max assumed 
temperature and do not show the ATM button.  In this case, the user would 

   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 66 
enter -2 in this box and remove the ATM  button in Step 6 of 10: Takeoff 
Layout - View/Define options for selected buttons. 
• Allow crew to turn off Obstacle Limit Calculations 
o For Part 91 operators, obstacles may be ignored when operating in visual 
meteorological conditions.  Selecting this option and adding the appropriate 
button to enable the crew to select this option in OPT will allow this. 
• Allow crew to enable CG check against curtailed ALT CG 
o This option will perform a check between the crew  entered CG(%) in the 
input box against the selected Alternate CG selection in the ALT CG button.  
Selecting this option and creating the appropriate button to enable the 
selections of Alternate CG in “Step 6 of 10: Takeoff Layout - View/Define 
options for selected buttons.” will allow this.   The user must also defined 
the CG Curtailed Value for the two Alternate CG options selected when 
defining the button in Step 6. 
• Include Clearway and Stopway in Takeoff Calculation 
o Selecting this option will include cle arway and stopway in the takeoff 
calculation. 
• Allow crew to calculate limits for multiple intersections 
o Selecting this option will enable the use of the INTX button in OPT, which 
is used to calculate results for both the full length of the runway and up to 
three additional  intersections at the same time ( ALL intersections are 
calculated when using either iPad or Windows 10 apps). 
• Include ALL or First 4 option in INTX button 
o Selecting this option will keep the choice to run all intersections at once.  
Unchecking the box, will only calculate the results for the full or the 
intersection selected. 
• Include Lineup Distance in the Calculation 
o Selecting this option will include lineup allowances in the takeoff 
calculation 
• Allow credit for grooved runway surface 
o Selecting this option will apply grooved/skid-resistant runways takeoff 
performance if supported by both the takeoff performance database and 
the runway definition.  Unchecking this option will eliminate credit for 
skid-resistant runways. 
• Define V1 Policy as Ratio of V1 min and V1 max 
o Selecting this option will make OPT publish an arithmetic average V1 value 
between a valid minimum and maximum. In order to use this option, you 
must have the V1 policy set to “Optimum” in the Manage Takeoff Policy 

 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 67 
section earlier in this chapter.  Valid inputs for %V1 Min to V1 Max Ratio 
are 1 – 100.  For example, an input of 50 means halfway between minimum 
and maximum V1. 
• Allow crew to use calculated windshear guidance 
o Selecting this option will enable the View/Edit Windshear Text button 
immediately below this check box.  The windshear guidance option places 
a windshear option on the OPT takeoff thrust rating button.  Selecting that 
button will display the windshear guidance information that is entered.  The 
user may customize that information to better suit their unique operational 
requirements and save those changes.  OPT will display this information 
when the crew chooses  WINDSHEAR.  OPT will also calculate a 
“windshear” Vr (one that has been increased by up to 20 kts) to assis t the 
crew in following standard windshear training.  This windshear Vr will also 
be displayed in the OPT output area, but in amber.  When Windshear and 
OPTIMUM flap is selected, OPT will use the recommended Windshear flap 
from the Takeoff Safety Training Aid if performance allows.  
If the Climbout configuration has been enabled, a new section called All Engine Settings 
is shown.   
 
The following options are available. 
• Allow crew to calculate engine-out gradients at altitude or distance 
o Selecting this option will allow the flight crew to enter an altitude or 
distance where the engine has failed after an all engine takeoff .  From this 
point on, an engine failure profile is flown. (OPT 4.40 and higher) 
• Enable All Engine Gradient Entry 
o Selecting this option will add a button call AEG in OPT Takeoff All Engine.  
This button will allow flight crews to either select a pre-defined All Engine

• Enable Climb Derates
