In the Landing Settings Section, there are settings to adjust the  calculated landing 
distance, based both on user-defined parameters and also on factors described in EASA 
AIR-OPS. 
• Landing Distance Factor 
o Selecting this option will adjust the computed landing enroute distances by 
the given amount. For example, if airline policy requires adding 15% of the 
actual distance for landing, input 1.15 in this field.  The computed landing 
distance is the landing distance as discussed in the Manage 
Dispatch/Enroute Landing Runway Condition/Crosswinds section. 
• Minimum Landing Distance Increment 
o Selecting this option will adjust the computed landing enroute distances by 
the given additional runway length for those cases when the Landing 
Distance Factor discussed above is less than this increment. For example, if 
airline policy requires a minimum of 500 ft or 15% be added to the actual 
distance for landing, one would enter 500 into this field and 1.15 into the 
Landing Distance Factor field . The computed landing distance is the 
landing distance as discussed in the Manage Dispatch/Enroute  Landing 
Runway Condition/Crosswinds section. 
  


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 69 
• Allow VREF Increment for Dispatch 
o Enabling this option will display a Vref entry box on the Landing Dispatch 
page to account for Vref additives when calculating maximum landing 
weight.  This option is only su pported for “AFM -DPI” models (777 and 
later) and is not required by regulations. 
• Apply CAT.POL.A.230/235 Landing Factor 
o Selecting this option will apply a 15% landing distance factor to all non -
dry/non-wet landing field lengths. 
• Enable Go-Around Gradient Calculation 
o Selecting this option will trigger an option in the landing calculation to 
calculate a limiting weight based a minimum go-around gradient.  This 
option also requires the presence of the correct gradient calculation file 
(goAround.sdb).  Starting with OPT version 4.60, the ability to use first 
principle performance when calculating go-around gradient limit weights 
was added.  AFM-DPI certified models can now use the data directly from 
the landing module.  Airplanes that are not using AFM-DPI databases but 
have the All Engine enabled can use the BCOP database for the go-around 
limit weight calculations.  Airplanes that do not meet either criteria will 
continue to use the second principle digitized performance from the 
goaround.sdb. Further information on this may be obtained from Boeing.   
• Comply with CAT.POL.A.230/235(e) 
o Selecting this option will enable the landing dispatch calculation to comply 
with CAT.POL.A.230/235(e), which states that the landing weight on the 
expected runway with expected winds does not exceed the landing weight 
on the most favorable runway in zero wind conditions.  
• Show both if CAT.POL.A.230/235(e) is limiting  
o This option will become enabled if Comply with 
CAT.POL.A.230/235(e) was checked.  If this option is left unchecked, 
OPT will continue to function as before and only display the most limiting 
dispatch landing limit weight including the most favorable limit weight.  If 
the user checks this option and the calculation is limited by the most 
favorable runway, then OPT will display two dispatch landing limit 
weights: one for the Most Favorable Runway and the second limit weight 
is the dispatch limit weight for the selected runway. 
• Apply landing factors and increments to NNC 
o Selecting this option will apply the landing factors and increments to the 
non-normal configuration calculations, in addition to the normal 
configuration calculations.  Unchecking this option allows the administrator 
to set up a situation where normal configs are factored and NNCs are not, 
similar to the recommendations in the TALPA ARC agreement. 

   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 70 
• Treat runway increment as part of flare distance for NNC 
o This is applicable to MLAS databases that do not support the FLARE 
distance variable RWYDL(8).  Selecting this option will treat  the runway 
increment as part of the flare distance for the non- normal configurat ion 
calculations.   Unchecking this option will use the flare distance calculated 
directly from the database and can be shorter than the recommended 
TALPA-ARC. 
• Allow credit for grooved runway surface 
o Selecting this option will apply grooved/skid-resistant runways 
performance if supported by both the performance database and the 
runway definition.  Unchecking this option will eliminate credit for skid-
resistant runways. 
 
• Enable Send Enroute Landing results to FD Pro (for ORE/BTE) 
o Selecting this option will allow OPT to send Enroute Landing results to FD 
Pro.  In order for this output option to show when selecting Send Output the 
user must also have FD Pro installed on the same iPad device as OPT.  In 
order for the functionality to fully work, the user must have the Airport 
Moving Map (AMM) and the FD Pro version must have this option supported.      
 
Clicking on the Next Step -> button will display Step 4 on the following screen.

The Optional Weight Decrement section applies only to airlines who are operating with 
items such as modifications that are not covered in the AFM or other source.  The user 
can enter penalties associated with those items here, and the fields should be left blank if 
they do not apply to your aircraft. 
In the General Settings group at the bottom of this screen, selections are made for: 
• Allow crew to enter temporary Airport Information 
o Selecting this button will display a button to allow the crew to enter 
temporary airport information.  There can be one temporary takeoff and one 
temporary landing airport created.  Any temporary airports that are entered 
are deleted the next time the application is launched. 
  


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 72 
• Allow use of Virtual Keyboard for input 
o Selecting this button enables the display of a virtual keyboard for those 
installations that may not have a convenient hard-keyboard. 
• Enable Auto popup Feature for Virtual Keyboard 
o This option will cause the virtual keyboard to automatically appear when an 
input field is selected and ready for entry. 
• Clear all selected MEL/CDL items on program initialization 
o Selecting this item will clear all active MEL/CDL items when the program 
launches. 
• Allow crew to enter CG position 
o Selecting this item will display an entry box for the crew to enter center  of 
gravity position to aid in the calculation of stab trim.   This option will also 
be automatically checked if “A llow crew to enable CG check against 
curtailed ALT CG” was selected in Step 3. 
• Clear all temporary NOTAM on program initialization 
o Selecting this option will clear all temporary NOTAM information when 
the program launches. 
• Allow crew to enter temporary NOTAM 
o Selecting this item will display a button to allow the crew to enter temporary 
NOTAM information such as runway shortening or temporary obstacles.  
This information is retained until deleted so that the information is not 
required to be constantly re-entered.  This information is used in addition to 
any time-effective NOTAM information that has been entered through the 
airport database. 
• Allow crew to disable time-effective NOTAM 
o Selecting this item will add a button to the ACTIVE NOTAMS page which 
will present a dialog box to the  crew for selectively enabling or disabling 
NOTAMs that were created in Administrator.  (The ACTIVE NOTAMS 
page is accessed from the AIRPORT INFO screen.) 
• Allow grooved runway NOTAM 
o This option will allow the crew to enter a temporary NOTAM which 
removes credit for grooved/skid-resistant runways (if applicable). 
• Enable Version Information Button 
o This is a Windows 7 onl y feature.  Selecting this option will enable the 
Enter label to display on Version Info button  text button immediately 
below this check box.  The user may customize the label of the button.  This 
option will add a button that displays the information for the OPT databases 
used.   

 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 73 
In the Narrow Runway Minimum Settings group at the bottom of this screen, selections 
are made to account for both narrow runway performance available in the SCAP database 
as well as to specify a runway width to switch to narrow takeoff runway crosswinds when 
that option is used.  The settings are as follows: 
• Width Type 
o Selecting either “SCAP” or “width” will instruct OPT as to whether your 
SCAP database uses a special SCAP setting or runway width to trigger the 
narrow runway performance. 
o Selecting “SCAP V1MCG Increment” will instruct OPT to use the SCAP 
database setting SPIA(30) to increase the calculated V1 limited by V
MCG by 
the value specified under Width SCAP Increment (kts). 
o  Selecting “SCAP V1MCG Factor” will instruct OPT to u se the SCAP 
database setting SPIA(29) to multiply the calculated V1 limited by VMCG by 
the value specified under Width SCAP Factor. 
• Width Unit 
o Select “Meters” or “Feet” as appropriate to your value specified in Width 
Trigger 
• Width Trigger 
o The width of the runway below which narrow runway effects are accounted 
for. 
• Width SCAP 
o Set “30 -Meter” if your SCAP database has specific 30 -meter runway 
performance or “Normal” otherwise. 
o Factor or Increment are shown if the proper Width Type is selected. 
 Note:  It is important to recognize that there may be some settings hidden below 
the original view.  If there is a scroll bar, one should scroll down to see the entire list 
of items available for selection to verify proper settings.

 Note:  Selecting the appropriate Flight Deck Display Text can be important, both in terms 
of better recognition by the flight crew, as well as some OPT dependencies.  In the 
case of the takeoff thrust button, the Flight Deck Display text for each of the ratings 
should be “TO”, “TO 1”, and “TO 2” for full rate, derate 1, and derate 2 respectively 
(or “TO-1” and “TO-2” as appropriate for your model).  This not only matches what 
is shown on the flight deck displays, but that label is also repeated in the output section 
in the context of reduced thrust, e.g. “D-TO 1”. 
 
 It is also important to note that if the nomenclature above is not followed, the Vspeeds 
transfer function on the 787 EFB will not function correctly.

Click on the Edit Display Layout  button on the lower left portion of the takeoff layout

This step is used to define what button and entry boxes are available to the end user.  The 
major sections on this screen are used to address the major sections on the OPT  input 
screens, namely the Airport section,  the Takeoff section, the Weight CG Layout (takeoff 
only) and the Landing Section (although not shown in the above graphic).  In each case, 
the options that are to be displayed to the OPT  user are located in the list box on the right 
side of the screen, while the available options are shown in the list boxes on the left side of 
the screen.  In the case of the Airport Layout section, there is only one option that may be 
removed or added – the intersection button that is used to select an intersection when 
available.  Because this is part of the standard input layout, it is automatically included 
when creating the input layout. 
In each of the sections show above, note that there is a smaller list box just to the left of 
the Selected Options list box.  This list box shows the label that is positioned next to the 
button or edit box on the OPT  display.  To update this label, or to move  the option up or 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 79 
down in the list, click on it to select it and then either update the label in the Update Label 
edit box (and then click on Update Label), or move the option using the arrows on the right 
side of the screen.  This is what this portion of the screen looks like when the Intersection 
option is selected. 
 
One can also use the arrows at the left to move a selected item from one list to the other.  
In this case, the left arrow could be used to move the Intersection option to the left box, 
thereby removing it from the OPT display. 
In the case of the takeoff and landing sections, each list box on the right lists the suggested 
input options, while the list box on the left lists those SCAP options that remain available 
(this varies with database).  Neither of these lists are populated until one selects a takeoff 
or landing configuration from the appropriate pull down menu.  
The functionality of these layout sections is the same as noted above in the Airport Layout 
section.  One selects an item in the left or right list box and then clicks on either the left or 
right arrow to move it from list to list.  The items in the right list box may be moved up or 
down by selecting one and then using the up and down arrows, and the labels may  be 
changed using the Update Label button as described above. 
The Weight CG Layout (takeoff only) is available for takeoff only and allows you to move 
the position of the Takeoff Weight (TOW), Zero Fuel Weight (ZFW) and CG.  For 
example, if your crew reads from a Load Sheet that reports ZFW first and then TOW, you 
might want to place the ZFW first and TOW second.    
One thing to consider when creating the OPT layout that includes both takeoff and landing 
is to position the buttons that have common purpose in the same place on each layout.  For 
instance, in most cases both the takeoff and landing will have a flaps selection button.  To 
avoid inadvertent user errors, these buttons should be situated in the same vertical location 
in both the takeoff and landing layouts.  That means  that if one decides to remove 
something like the ATM entry box, then one should replace it with a blank area using the 
–SPACE- option in the left list box, thereby retaining the same vertical position for those 
options under it in the right list box.

takeoff layout page (Step 6), which will allow you to preview what you have done.

For Step 8a, the following window is displayed: 
 
Note the scroll bar on the right (if present). You may have to scroll down to see the entire 
contents on your display. 
On this screen, there are several elements that are set up for the final W&B definition for 
this Build ID.  Many of these parameters, in a manner similar to other policy sections, 
require an in -depth knowledge of the subject matter and company loading system.  The 
upper left corner, the Mean Aerodynamic Chord (MAC) section, contains all of the 
parameters that are used to set up the c.g. and index equations.  These equations may be 
written as (balance arm is denoted as BA): 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 83 
%MAC = 100 * (BA –BA leading edge) / (length of MAC) 
index = (weight * (BA –BA reference position)) / (c.g. moment) + index adjustment 
These terms are typically obtained from your W&B manual or loading system 
substantiation document.  Clicking on the Get MAC Default Settings  button will 
retrieve the standard Boeing settings for each airplane. 
The check box for Display Data in %MAC will, if checked, will cause OPT to display 
W&B information on its graph in %MAC, rather than index. 
In the Operational Empty Weight section in the middle left-hand-side, any OEW & BA 
that were previously defined in the Administrator in  Step 3 of 10: Set Airplane operational 
weights, takeoff and landing settings will be populated here. The weight units are the same 
as used in Step 3 .  This section will not be present if the user selects to activate the 
Advanced W&B option.         
In the Misc. Weight & Balance Settings section at the lower left, checking the Allow Last 
Minute Items in Weight and Balance info  check box will allow the crew to input LMC 
items on the third tab of the W&B screen.  The users will need to have the weight and 
moment arm information for each item input.  Also in this section are options to cause OPT 
to clear all W&B entries when a new airport is selected, as well as allow the OPT user to 
save and restore the current entries in the W&B module.  This latter option is a convenient 
way to store and retrieve a standard configuration if that is part of your operation. 
In the upper right corner of the screen, in the Fuel Density section, there are inputs to 
specify the default fuel density used.  This is the information that the flight deck application 
uses to relate fuel capacity to fuel weight.  Use the Allow Crew to Change Fuel 
Density check box to allow the crew to override the default value on this screen. 
In the center, right hand section of this screen, the Fuel Tank Selection section, the tanks 
are specified from a list of tanks previously created in the Manage Weight and Balance  
portion of the Administrator.  In addition, because some airplanes have auxiliary tanks or 
several tanks that have a more complicated  fuel usage schedule, the software has the 
capability to use a special loading procedure that is coded in the OPT application.  The 
following names should be used in the Customized Fuel DLL name: entry box: 
BBJs (-700/-800/-900 & MAX): fuelbbj2tank 
747-200/-300: fuel742 
747-400-/400F: fuel744 
747-8/-8F: fuel748 
757-200: fuel757fun 
Contact Boeing Flight Operations Engineering if you have a need for this functionality and 
the model is not listed above.

On this screen, if you’d like a different OPT  label for the passenger s creen tab, you can

The Passenger Types : table provides a drop down list of passenger types previously  
defined in the Manage Weight & Bal ance area.  OPT supports up to five (5)  passenger 
types (OPT v4.50 & higher).  Next to each passenger type, decide if the number entered is 
counted in the total number of passengers in a given zone by checking the Count in Zones: 
checkbox.  For instance, some airlines do not count infants against the seat count in a given 
zone because they are sitting on the parents lap . The Allow to Edit Weight : column, if 
checked, enables the flight crew to change/enter  a weight allowance for that particular 
passenger type.

When multiple envelopes are used with multiple dependencies, it is good to plan these 
entries in a manner that flows from the most restrictive set of requirements to least 
restrictive.  OPT will read through the list of restrictions in the order input and display the 
first one that is true.

This screen provides a ll the inputs required to describe the operational curtailments that 
will be displayed within OPT as a shaded band, similar to the image shown here.  Most 
inputs are labeled on the image to assist you in entering the correct values.  There are 
curtailments for non-passenger related items (points 1-4), and a fuel burn value (item 7) to 
specify the amount of fuel that is burned during takeoff and initial climb, before the 
passengers begin moving about the cabin, and passenger-related curtailments that must be 
considered.  The passenger -related curtailments (points 5 -6) are divided into two 
categories: a smaller curtailment below a specified number of passengers, and a larger 
curtailment above that count.  This passenger count trigger value is the first item in the list 
on the left side of this screen.  Once all values have been input, click on Save to close this 
window and return to the Step 9a screen.

For OPT Application Configuration Settings, the options on the above screen are as 
follows: 
• Allow Takeoff Details page to be Displayed 
o When there is takeoff data available in OPT, this option will display a button 
on the airport info screen in OPT called Takeoff Details that will display a 
summary screen of  secondary information pertinent to the takeoff data 
currently displayed.  Note that, in general, this information is of little use to 
flight crew and should be used mainly for back-office purposes. 
o Display Limit Weights  – if checked, under the Takeoff Det ails screen a 
summary of the limit weights for field, obstacle, climb, tire speed and return 
to land (if applicable) will be displayed.  
!! Caution!  Display of the Takeoff Details page in the Onboard Performance 
Tool may lead the crew to make erroneous as sumptions pertaining to a 
particular takeoff.  Data displayed on this page is provided as information 
only and should not be used to otherwise modify proper takeoff procedure 
and technique.  The data displayed should not be used to make decisions 
regarding runway usage. 
o Display Obstacle Clearance Margin  – if checked, under the Takeoff 
Details screen a summary table of the obstacles will be displayed with the 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 103 
height, distance and clearance margin for each obstacle.   The o bstacle 
clearance (Clrnc.) displayed by OPT includes required regulatory margin.    
• Allow Landing Details page to be Displayed 
o When there is landing data available in OPT , this option will display a 
button on the airport info screen in OPT  called Landing Details that will 
display a summary screen of secondary information pertinent to the landing 
data currently displayed. 
• Allow Takeoff Graphics to be Displayed 
o If checked, this option will display the takeoff graph pertinent to the takeoff 
data currently displayed in OPT after a takeoff speeds calculation.  If the 
takeoff graph is not desired, uncheck this box.  In the iPad a toggle Rwy 
Graphic switch was introduced to toggle between the numerical results and 
the graph. 
• Allow All Engine (Climbout) Graphics to be Displayed 
o If checked, this option will display the All Engine graph pertinent to the all 
engine data currently displayed in OPT after a calculation.  If the All Engine 
graph is not desired, uncheck this box.  In the iPad a toggle Climb Graphic 
switch was introduced to toggle between the numerical results and the 
graph. 
• Allow both factored and unfactored distances to be Displayed 
o This option is only available on the iPad and Windows 10 App versions  at 
this time.  If checked, this option will display in the landing enroute output 
a toggle button Factored/Unfactored where the user can toggle the 
numerical results and the graph for the landing enroute distances.  The 
values used for factored data depend on factors defined in Step 3 of 10: Set 
Airplane operational weight s, takeoff and landing se ttings and/or Manage 
Enroute Landing Runway Conditions/Crosswinds under Manage Policy & 
Config Options.   
o Non-Normal Landing distances results are only displayed in one category 
at this time.  The result for the NNL depends on the choice selected in Step 
3 of 10: Set Airplane operational weights, takeoff and landing settings : 
Apply landing factors and increments to NNC selection. 
o “Factored Header Label:” & “Unfactored Header Label:” 
• These become enabled when Allow both factored and unfactored 
distances to be Displayed is checked.  The user has the option to 
change the labels displayed by OPT on the output screen by typing 
a new header label for each option.  
 
 

   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 104 
• Enable Compare Calculations 
o iPad only.  If checked, this option will display a Compare Calculation option 
under the Actions menu.  In OPT this will become enabled only after a 
calculation has been completed.  This feature is meant to aid in the cross -
check of the data calculated. (OPT v 4.50 & higher). 
• Initial Runway Intersection Button Label 
o This button allows the administrator to define a default selection of the 
runway intersection button that is used when OPT encounters a runway in 
the airport database that has intersections.  Allowable inputs are none, full, 
and first 4, corresponding to no default selection (require crew input), full 
(just select the full length runway calculation), and calculate answers for the 
full length runway and up to 3 intersections.  In the mobile applications 
there is no restriction to the number of intersections calculated so instead of 
first 4 the application shows All .  If the user selected to not include the 
ability to run all intersections at once in 
Step 3 of 10: then the only allowable 
inputs are none and full.

• Enable Printing  
o Enables a button to support sending data to a Windows® printer or a printer 
that supports Air Print for an iPad. 
• Enable printing to non-AirPrint printers 
o Allows an iPad user to generate a PDF file of the output and send to a non-
AirPrint printer. 
• Enable Printing of EOP

• Enable Printing of Runway Comments 
o Enables a button to support printing of information from the Runway

o This option is present if W&B is active.  Enables the option to support 
printing W&B Loadsheet to a PDF file. 
• Hide 'Send Separate or Combined e-Mail' Dialog notice:  
o This option allows the back office Administrator to default the setting and 
hide the prompt presented to the user that asks how to send multiple emails 
if multiple emails are selected under the SEND Output option.  
• Combined – combines multiple emails into one 
• Separate – sends separate emails for each output selected. 
• Allow Output Data to be Sent to Text File 
o Enables a button (the same button as the printing button) to support sending 
data to a text file.

Page 106 
• Enable capability to save LDI Vspeed uplink message 
o Enables a button to create and save a standard LDI takeoff speeds uplink 
message to a pre-defined directory.  This potentially allows the operator to 
write an application that scans this directory frequently, transmits the 
message to a ground station for further up- linking back to the airplane’s 
FMS.  
 Note:  For this function to work properly, the selections on the takeoff thrust 
rating selection button must start with some variation of the standard flight deck 
nomenclature, such as TO, TO-1, TO 1, etc. 
• Sends data to Data Storage 
o Enables a button (the same button as the printing button) to support sending 
summary data from the current calculation to an existing text file to enable 
record keeping. 
• Print the Takeoff Bug Card 
o This will allow the user to include the takeoff bug card in the printed output 
sent to a Windows
® printer. 
• Preview Bug Card 
o This will allow the user to display on the screen a representation of the bug 
card using the Send Output button. 
• Enable Crew Signing 
o This will allow the user to digitally sign the output before sending to the 
desired location.  If   a crewdatafile.ini file is provided to the application 
then the file will be signed as follows “Signed by Captain Crew ID at 
Time Stamp on date-month-year”.  If no file is provided but this option is 
enabled, the output file is signed as follows: “Signed by Captain (NOT 
AUTHENTICATED) Crew ID at Time Stamp on date-month-year.   
Please reference the OPT Crew Roster File Specifications (available in 
MBF under OPT Support Materials) for details on how to generate a file 
with encrypted passwords supported by OPT.    
• Hide Crew Data 
o If Enable Crew Signing is activated, the Administrator will have the 
option to hide on the screen the list of the crew if this is selected.  The 
crew will have to know their name or Crew ID to be able to authenticate.   
• Enable Takeoff Trace 
o Triggers an option to automatically record trace data for every takeoff 
calculation made

• Enable Landing Trace 
o Triggers an opt ion to automatically record trace data for every landing 
calculation made. 
• Days before Deleting Trace Files 
o This is the number of days that trace files will be kept.  The application will 
delete any trace files created before that time to help save space. 
• Minutes before clearing inputs when in background 
o This entry is to input the amount of time in minutes before the inputs are 
cleared from OPT after remaining idle in the background.  The application 
has a default of 180 minutes (OPT v 4.50 & higher). 
• Reset to Aircraft (Tail) Selection Menu: 
o This option will allow the user to change the reset of the OPT takeoff 
selection screen when the above idle time is reached.  Currently, the default 
is to reset to the current selected aircraft.  This option, if checked, will reset 
OPT to the Select Aircraft main menu when multiple tails are present.  (OPT 
v 4.90 & higher). 
• Force update(s) when new data is available: 
o For those that use the OPT data delivery from the Distribution Mana ger 
(BDM or JDM Pro), this option, if checked, will force the OPT data update 
on the user.  The current functionality is to alert the user via the red circle 
and the user will perform the update when desired.  (OPT v 4.90 & higher). 
• Specify snooze time (in minutes) for new data download alerts: 
o If “Force update(s) when new data is available:” above is checked and this 
time is set to “0”, the OPT updates will be forced immediately to the user.  
The user cannot use OPT unless the update takes place.  If a time other than 
“0” (zero) is specified, a n alert will be provided every “X” minutes that 
updates are available and the user needs to update.  (OPT v 4.90 & higher).

Printing Airplane Summary Information  
The Administrator application has the capability to print summary information for each 
Build ID listed on the Build ID List on the Create Policy Definition Screen.  When a Build 
ID is selected in the Build ID list box, the Print Summary  button is active.  When this 
button is clicked on, Administrator creates a .pdf file listing summary information for the 
Build ID.  The user is free to print or save this file as desired.

Airport Management 
Airport Management is likely to be the most frequently used part of the  Administrator 
unless your airline has a process for managing the airport data file outside of the 
application.  Airport data may be manually entered and edited within the Administrator, or 
the Administrator can import airport data from any of the formatte d file selections 
discussed in this section. 
The home page for the Airport Management function is shown below.  It is shown with 
one airport selected in the Airport list box.  When an airport is selected, this screen will 
show the airport elevation, available runways, and any comments that have been entered 
for this airport. 
 
At this point, the available functions are as follows: 
• Find (above the airport list box) 
o Typing the airport 4-letter ICAO code into the entry box and clicking on 
this button will takeoff you to and select that airport 


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 114 
• New (under the airport list box) 
o This button will open a new window to create and input data for a new 
airport. 
• Edit (under the airport list box) 
o This button will open the editing window for the selected airport 
• Delete…  (under the airport list box) 
o This button will open a new window to guide the user through the airport 
delete process 
• New (under the Runway list box) 
o This button will open a new window to create and input data for a new 
runway for the selected airport.   
• Edit (under the Runway list box) 
o This button will open the editing window for the selected runway.  This 
button is only active when there is a runway selected. 
• Delete (under the Runway list box) 
o This button will delete the currently selected runway after confirmation 
from the user.  This button is only active when there is a runway selected. 
• Version Identifier (20 char)  
o This text entry field is used to store an airport database version identifier.  
This version ID may be output to the OPT main screen to validate 
database effectivity. 
• Import Airport file 
o This button will open a new window to start the airport import function 
described next. 
• Print Airport 
o This button will open a new window to enable the user to print a summary 
of one or multiple airports 
• Save 
o When changes to information on this screen have been made, such as to 
the version ID, this button becomes active and allows the user to save 
those changes. 
When a runway in the runway list box has been selected, the Airport Management home 
page will then display a summary of the information for that runway, an example of 
which is shown below.  As noted above, to edit or change any of the information for this 
runway, one would click on the Edit button under the runway list box.

Importing Airports  
Importing airports is probably the singular most used action in the Administrator  
application.  Currently, Administrator supports the importing of airport files in the Boeing 
STAS format or the IATA SCAP Airport Data Interchange format v3 or later .  I mport 
filters for other airport data formats may be available in the future.  
 
 Note:  Users of the IATA SCAP Airport Data Interchange format must have files 
that comply with the Boeing-supplied schema for this format.  The schema may 
be obtained from the MBF Performance Software General Airplane Information 
heading under OPT Support Material. 
 
The following steps are used to import airport data from an airport data file: 
1. Starting from the Airport Management Screen , click the Import Airp ort File 
button at the bottom of the page, which will display the following screen. 
 
 
2. On the Import Airport screen, click the Browse… button to navigate to a STAS -
formatted airport data file on your local hard drive or network.   
3. From the pull -down menu on the right, select either STAS file Type  or IATA 
SCAP  XML file Type, as appropriate for your data format. 
4. Click Continue to import the airports in the STAS airport file into the application. 
5. The module will display the screen shown below .  Note that the airports from the 
STAS airport file are displayed in the Available Airports to Import list. 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 117 
 
6. Select the airports from the Available list that you wish to include in the OPT airport 
database. You can add airports to the Airports to Import  list using any of the 
following methods: 
• Select a SINGLE airport: click the desired airport and use the single (right 
pointing) arrow button. 
• Select ALL airports: click the double arrow (right pointing) button. 
• Selecting more than one airport: hold down the CTRL key while selecting the 
desired airports.  Use the single arrow button to move them to the import list. 
To remove airports from the import list, use the same methods noted above but with 
the reverse (left pointing) single or double arrow buttons. 
 
7. Select the radio button corresponding to the Import Type desired: 
• Insert/Update:  This option will update the airports already loaded in the 
database and insert new airports with the data from the import file.  The 
following rules are applied:   
1. If the selected import airport is not in the database , then import the airport 
and runway data from STAS file. 
2. If the selected import airport is in the database, then delete all existing data 
associated with the airport from the database (runways, obstacles, 


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 118 
intersections, and NOTAMs), and import the airport and runway data from 
the STAS file. 
• Replace: This option will update the airports already loaded in the database 
with the data from the import file.  Airports in the import file that have not been 
previously loaded into the database will be ignored.  The followi ng rules are 
applied: 
1. If the selected import airport is not currently in the database, then s kip 
airport and do not modify database.  
2. If the selected import airport is currently in the database, then delete 
all existing data associated with the airport from the database 
(runways, obstacles, intersections, and NOTAMs), and import the 
airport and runway data from the STAS file. 
• New (Overwrite): This option will delete all existing data then add all the 
airports/runways from the data file.  In all cases the following rules apply: 
1. Delete all existing data from the database (airport, runway, obstacles, 
intersections, and NOTAM’s), and import all selected airports and 
runways from the STAS file 
 
Once you’ve selected the airports to import and the import type, click the Import 
button to save them to the Administrator database.  If there are a large number of 
airports in the database, it could take a few minutes to update the database. 
  

 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details.

Editing Existing Airport Information  
The airport editing function is not just used to change information, but to also add 
information such as airport comments.  To edit existing airport information, simply select 
and airport in the Airport list box and click on the Edit  button to display the following 
screen. 
 
This screen allows the user to add or change any of the information currently in effect for 
the selected airport.  Note that if one elects to change the reference units from the currently 
selected values, then the Administrator will display another screen asking the user whether 
or not to convert the existing data to the new units.  Once all desired changes have been 
made, click on the Save  button to save the changes and return to the previous screen.  
Clicking on the Cancel  button will discard any changes that have been made pr ior to 
returning to the previous screen.

Editing Existing Runway Information  
The runway editing function is used to add or change existing information, as well as to 
add time effective NOTAM information.  To edit existing runway information, select a 
runway in the Runway list box and click on the Edit button.  The following screen is then 
displayed. 
 
The items on this screen are as follows: 
• Runway 
o Allows the user to change or append additional characters to the runway ID.  
OPT runways must follow standa rd runway nomenclature, e.g. the first 2 
characters must be the runway numerical designation, with an optional third 
character for left, center, or right.  All other trailing characters are optional 
user-defined descriptive characters. 
• Mag Hdg 
o Allows the u ser to input an accurate magnetic heading for the runway.  
When this is done, instead of converting the runway ID to magnetic heading 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 121 
for headwind/crosswind purposes, OPT will use this input magnetic 
heading.  An entry of zero will cause OPT to convert the  runway ID to 
magnetic heading for its purposes. 
• Distance: 
o Length – depending on how the units/references are specified for this 
particular airport, this distance will either be runway length, or Takeoff Run 
Available (TORA) 
o Clearway - depending on how the  units/references are specified for this 
particular airport, this distance will either be clearway, or Takeoff Distance 
Available (TODA) 
o Stopway - depending on how the units/references are specified for this 
particular airport, this distance will either be  stopway, or Accelerate Stop 
Distance Available (ASDA) 
o LDA – landing distance available 
• %Slope: 
o Runway slope for the accelerate-go, and accelerate-stop for takeoff, and the 
landing distance available (LDA) 
• Runway Width 
o This input is optional and is used by  those operators who wish to trigger a 
narrow runway performance option.  When this runway width is less than 
the threshold value set by the airline, the performance adjustments for a 
narrow runway will be used. 
• Runway Status 
o Allow runway for takeoff – If checked, the runway is to be used for takeoff 
o Allow runway for landing – If checked, the runway is to be used for landing. 
o Runway meets skid resistance criteria –  If checked, the runway meets the 
skid resistant maintenance criteria, such as a well -maintain grooved 
runway. 
• Lineup Distance 
o No Lineup Allowance –  to be used when the runway does not require a 
lineup allowance 
o Use 90 Degree Turn Data – the information stored in the airplane policy 
database for a 90 degree turn should be used 
o Use 180 Degree Turn D ata – the information stored in the airplane policy 
database for a 180 degree turn should be used 
o Optionally specified entry angle – enter an entry angle that matches one of 
the optional angles that have been specified in the airplane policy database

DDG Management 
OPT uses a database to maintain all of the performance-related Minimum Equipment List 
(MEL) and Configuration Deviation List (CDL) penalties as listed in the combined Boeing 
document, commonly known as the Dispatch Deviations Guide (DDG), or Dispatch 
Deviations Procedure Guide (DDPG).  The OPT administrator is allowed to customize this 
information in a ma nner similar to how an airline would manage their own “company 
DDG.” Administrator uses a master database that Boeing creates for each airplane and 
engine combination and uses that as the Master DDG for the starting point for airline 
modifications.  This master DDG database file is directly downloadable from Boeing  via 
the MBF Performance Software page.  If there is no desire to customize the file, you can 
simply use the database you download from Boeing; this would then preclude the need to 
separately create the DDG data file discussed in a later section. If customization of the 
Boeing baseline is desired, Administrator users are allowed to change chapter and item 
titles and numbering, increase penalties for existing items, and add items of their own.  
The DDG Management home page is accessed by clicking on the DDG Management link 
in the site map on the left of each screen.  The home page for the DDG Management 
function is shown below. 
 
To import the Master DDG that you have downloaded from MBF, click on the Import 
DDG Master  button to present a standard Administrator file import screen.  Click on 
Import and Return to complete the process, which leaves one at the DDG Management 
home page which now looks like this: 
 
This screen will show a double -line entry for each Master DDG that is loaded.  The top 
line contains edit boxes for the Version ID and the DDG Document Title and are modifiable 
by the user.  The bottom line displays the master information as loaded by the Boeing 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 133 
DDG.  To further customize this DDG information for airline use, just click on the Edit 
link in the left- most column of the table.  That will cause the following screen to be 
displayed. 
 
On this screen, the DDG Chapter numbers and Chapter Titles may be changed, if desired.  
In addition, the user may enable or disable an entire chapter by using the check box in th e 
Enable column of the table.  If changes are made to information on this screen, clicking on 
the Save button at any time will save those changes and return one to the Manage DDG 
home page.  Clicking on Cancel will, of course, discard any changes that might have been 
made before returning to the Manage DDG home page.  For each of the chapters listed, 
one may click on the either the MEL  or CDL link to view or edit the information for that 
specific chapter.  For instance, when that is done for the MEL link, the following screen is 
displayed.  Note that this example will deal with the MEL portion of the database, but the 
CDL portion works in a similar fashion. 


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide

Page 134 
 
In this chapter level look at the DDG, one may change any of the item numbers or titles to

disabled using the check boxes in the Enable column of the table.

Creating Data Files 
Creating Data Files for Windows 7® Platforms 
Once all of the information that was developed in the preceding sections is in place, it is 
time to create each of the data files necessary for OPT to function properly.  There are 
four files involved; three that are SQLite database files, and one that is a text file used to 
describe to OPT the look and feel and options available on the user interface.  The 
technical details for these 4 files are included as reference material in the documentation 
folder in the OPT root directory and is installed with the OPT installer downloaded from 
MBF.   
 
 Note:  SQLite is a software library that implements a self-contained, serverless, zero-
configuration, transactional SQL database engine and is the most widely deployed database 
engine in the world.  If you have a need to examine the data, you can do so with the SQLite 
Database Browser, which is freeware that you can find by “Googling” “SQLite Database 
Browser”.  The SQLite database files normally have a “.sdb” file extension, but this is not 
required.  In fact, one should consider changing it to something else to help preclude the end 
user from recognizing the database format and taking steps to change the contents.  For 
instance, changing the .sdb file extension to .OPT would not infringe on OPT operation, but 
would more than likely inhibit other users from recognizing that it is a SQLite database. 
The three database files contain the airport data, airplane data, and DDG data. To access 
the Administrator functions that create these data files, click on the Create Data Files link

Creating Data Files for the iPad® or Windows 10® Devices  
Creating files for the iPad and Windows 10 (mobile) devices is very similar to creating 
files for Windows 7 computers except that there is also a means within the Administrator 
application to distribute the resultant files.  Because of this, there is an additional 
checkbox (Build using External Files) on the initial screen when creating mobile device 
files that allows the user to upload files that have been modified in order to put them back 
on the MBF server for transmission to the mobile device user community.  You can see 
this check box in the picture below:
 
 
The previous section explained how to create the files for Windows 7 computers.  Very 
similar same steps are used to create the policy, airport, configuration and ddg  for Mobile 
Content.  We must also create the Performance Part  (perf_perf), the optional Crew Data 
(perf_crewID), and the optional Nav Data part s (perf_navdata), using the “Build using 
External Files” option to complete the Mobile Content.  The databases for the Performance 
Part do not change very often so this step only needs to be done when there is a change to 
one of the components in perf_perf. To upload the performance databases (takeoff, landing 
and Climbout (if applicable)), the go -Around.sdb (if applicable), the StabTrim.sdb (if 
applicable) and secureCode2 for distribution in JDM Pro or BDM using the Administrator 
follow these steps. 
1) Gather the all the takeoff, landing and climbout (if using All Engine) 
databases for all the models that you want to send to the distribution 
group.  If the aircraft  is AFM-DPI certified: gather all the individual 
files with a .dbn extension (n = 1 or 2) and if appli cable also gather the 
non-normal database with a db extension.  For the 737-NG also include 


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 146 
the new brakecooling database.   If the airplane is certified with a paper 
Flight Manual:  gather files with a .bdb or .db extension and if applicable 
also gather the non-normal database with a db extension.  For the All-
Engine Climb feature, gather the climbout files  with the following 
extensions *.cnf, *dat, *lsp, *.opl, *.dir & *.nse.     
2) Gather the go -Around.sdb (if applicable), the StabTrim.sdb (if 
applicable) and secureCode2 files. 
3) Instead of loading each file individually, the user can create a zip file 
with all the components from 1 &  2 above.  The CAT/CAM and 
Administrator allow the user to upload a zip file and it will extract its 
contents and assign the sam e file type to all contents in this zip file.   
FYI, a ll files contained in this zip file must be of the same type  
(perf_perf).  When creating the zip file ensure that the files are zipped 
at the individual file level and not at the folder level. 
4) Select the check box for Build using External Files in ‘Step 1 of 3: 
Select Data Files to Create’  
5) In ‘Step 2 of 3: Select Data files to add to build package.’, upload the 
zip file created in step 3 above by navigating to the folder where the 
file is located 
6) Assign File Type “SCAP File” and click on the Next Step 
7) The next screen is the  Performance Build List for Mobile Device Data 
Files.

Roster File following the specifications provided in MyBoeingFleet, this  crewdatafile.ini 
file must be loaded using Build using External Files for further distribution to the OPT

3) Assign File Type “Crew Data” and click on the Next Step

Using the Distribution Manager 
The first step to getting access to the Distribution Manager is to gain access to it.  This is 
done by sending an email to CISCustomerSupport@boeing.com
.  You will be contacted 
by one of our EFB deployment managers who will guide you through the process of getting 
set up and opening up any accounts that need to be created. 
After that process is complete, you would then gain access to the Distribution Manager.  
This service can be accessed from the MBF homepage by clicking on the Mobile Gallery 
link in the center section of the home page.  Once that page is displayed, click on the 
Distribution Manager tab and log into that site with your new login credentials provided 
by your Deployment Manager .  Th e most up-to-date help material is available online by 
clicking on the welcome message at the top right of the Application toolbar and then 
clicking Help in the new window that appears.  There is also a pdf version of the help 
material available by selecting User Guides from the menu at top left of this new window.   
To set up the OPT Administrator side of the data distribution, you click on the BDM  
Grouping link in the left margin of the Administrator screen under Preferences.  That will 
display a new page  to enter the group names that you would have created on the 
Distribution Manager site.  Creating these groups will allow you to transfer your data 
directly from the Administrator to your users’ iPads with no intervening steps once it’s all 
set up.  Here’s a screen shot of what this looks like in the Administrator with one sample 
group added.   
 
To add more groups, you would simply click on the Add button to add another line.  
Clicking on the Save button will save your work and return you to the main screen. 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 151 
The first time you send a package of data to a group, you will need to log into the 
Distribution Manager to associate that data package with the Distribution Manager’s 
groups that you have created there.  After the first time, the Distribution Manager will make 
that association automatically and sends the data to your users.

o This automatically creates a multitail.xml file for the user based on the

o This automatically creates a multitail.xml file for the user based on two

o This automatically creates a multitail.xml file for the user based all their 
selectable configurations and there are no levels.  The user can save the file 
using the right hand corner SAVE button to their desired directory for later 
use.   
• View Multi-Tail XML File         
o This option allows the user to view an already created multitail.xml file.   
• Validate Multi-Tail XML File   
o This option allows the user to validate an already created multitail.xml file.  
This just validated that the structure is correct.

Chapter Five  
How to use the Onboard Performance 
Tool for Windows 7 
What it's for 
The Onboard Performance Tool application is intended to be an easy-to-use interface that 
produces airplane performance related data for the flight crew.  It is a Windows ® based 
application and makes use of an intuitive user interface.  It is assumed that prior to using 
the Onboard Performance Tool , the administrato r has set up airplane , airport, and DDG  
databases for the Onboard Performance Tool  user, the computer on which the Onboard 
Performance Tool has been installed has a correctly set up directory structure, and the 
Onboard Performance Tool  users are sufficient ly knowledgeable about the Windows ® 
operating system and typical user interfaces to accomplish the tasks. 
OPT may be set up to have many different appearances.  The two more common 
appearances are the standard Windows appearance or the same appearance as t he Boeing 
Class 3 Electronic Flight Bag (EFB).  Except for the initial splash screen and tail selection 
dialog box, all of the examples shown are from the Class 3 appearance, which is the Boeing 
recommended user interface (UI). 
Because OPT is a very easily  customizable application, your administrator may have 
created an appearance that differs in several ways from the examples shown in this chapter.  
Questions about these differences should be directed to your company administrator. 

   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 154 
Using the Onboard Performance Tool  
for Takeoff –Windows 7 
Depending on how your administrator has set up the application, OPT  may or may not 
display a “splash screen” when the application is launched  (double-clicked).  Similar to 
Administrator, the Onboard Performance Tool displays a splash screen until the user clicks 
somewhere on the picture, or presses the Enter  or Esc keys.  This splash screen might 
look like that shown below. 
 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 155 
If your OPT installation has more than one airplane tail or type loaded, then you will be 
presented with a list of tails, or airplanes, to choose from.  This list might look like that 
shown below. 
 
 
Select the applicable tail number or airplane description and then click on the Complete  
button to start OPT .  Once the Complete  button is clicked, the main crew screen for 
takeoff appears, entitled at the top of the page PERFORMANCE - TAKEOFF. 


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 156 
 
This screen may be used to describe three different types of input features; the pushbutton, 
the dropdown button, and the edit box.   
The pushbutton can be seen by looking at the airport search button, ARPT SEARCH.  
Pushbuttons are denoted by a gray button with a name and will either display a new screen 
when pushed, or accomplish some specific action.  In the case of ARPT SEARCH, a new 
screen will appear to perform an airport search function. 
Dropdown buttons look very similar to the pushbuttons, but have an arrow-like triangle on 
their right side to denote that further information will appear to the right of the button when 
pressed.  As an example, clicking on the A/C CONFIG button will display a list of air 
conditioning options to choose from that might look like this: 
 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 157 
To select the desired item, simply click on the menu item that is display ed.  Note that as 
the mouse device moves over the various selections, t here is a white “hover box” that 
appears over the active area.  To collapse the menu without making a selection, click on 
either the original A/C CONFIG button, or the EXIT button.  
The editbox can be seen with the WIND, OAT and QNH entries where the user is free to 
enter text. 
Color also plays an important part of the OPT Class 3-style UI.  In the main takeoff screen, 
shown above, there are buttons that are shown that are gray, and there are buttons that are 
shown that have a black interior with a cyan  outline.  The gray buttons are active buttons 
and the black buttons with cyan  outlines are inactive buttons.  As noted above, a white 
outline around a button or edit box means that that input device is the currently active 
screen element.  The need for this becomes more obvious when tabbing between elements.  
Lastly, the text on the buttons will turn green once action has been taken to make it evident 
that a selection has been made.  Once each button has a green label, and the required edit 
box inputs have been made, the CALC button will become active and the user may make 
a calculation based on the current inputs. 
The main crew screen, for the most part, is set up in three basic functional areas.  These 
areas are divided by cyan  group boxes.  The upper left portion is devoted mainly to crew 
input of airport and atmospheric information, the upper right portion is devoted to crew 
input of airplane configuration information, while the lower  portion is devoted to output 
and results .  Some buttons and/or input boxes  may not be available on your screen, 
depending on the airplane model and other options controlled by the administrator. 
Runway/Atmospheric Inputs 
As noted above, the crew input is mainly divided up into airport/atmospheric inputs and 
airplane configuration inputs.  The airport/atmospheric inputs would typically vary little 
between different OPT installations and consists at a minimum of the airport search button, 
the runway search button, and edit boxes for wind, OAT, and altimeter setting (QNH).  In 
addition, there is an optional button to make selections for intersection calculations.  Note 
that the tail number or configuration is also generally listed in the upper left corner of this 
area. 
Airport Search 
Clicking on the ARPT button will display the airport search screen.  This screen is shown 
below. 

   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 158 
 
In this example, “ks” was typed into the search edit box at the bottom and the SEARCH 
IDENT button was pushed, resulting in seven results being returned.  Four of the results 
are shown, with the remaining three being available on a second page of results.   Each of 
the buttons on this screen function as follows: 
• SEARCH IDENT 
o Will search for all airports that contain the search string (“ks”) in their 4 -
letter code. 
• SEARCH ALL 
o Will search for all airports that c ontain the search string in their 4 -letter 
code, 3-letter code, airport name, or city. 
• PREVIOUS/NEXT 
o If more than four ( 4) results are returned, NEXT will take the user to the 
next page.  Results are displayed in alphabetical order by 4 -letter code.  
PREVIOUS will return the user to the previous screen in order. 
• CANCEL 
o Will return the user to the main screen without making any changes to the 
previous state of the airport search button. 
• Results buttons 
o Up to four buttons are activated with the results that a re returned in the 
results area.  In the example above, these would be the buttons for KSAN, 
KSEA, KSFO, and KSJC.  Clicking on one of these buttons will select that 
airport for use on the main screen , will change the ARPT button name to 
the (green) 4-letter airport code, and will populate the runway button with 
the available runways. 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 159 
Entering the airport search function and selecting an airport for the takeoff screen will also 
affect data that is displayed on the takeoff screen.  Selecting an airport for takeoff will also 
clear the wind, OAT, QNH, and Weight and Balance information; the assumption being 
that calculations for a new flight are about to begin. 
If there is only one airport returned from the airport search, then OPT will assume that the 
correct airport was found and then automatically return to the main screen just like the user 
had selected that one airport in the results area.

name to the (green) runway ID, and check for existing intersection information in the 
airport database.  Cli cking on the original button or the EXIT  button will close the 
dropdown button with no changes.

Selecting Intersections (if available) 


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 160 
If your administrator has included intersection data in your airport database and, if there is 
intersection data available for the select ed runway, the INTX button will become active.  
A typical selection is shown below. 
 
Selecting “ALL” by clicking on the ALL button will calculate takeoff information for the 
full length runway (25RT) and each of the intersections (B1 and A2) in this case.  Selecting 
either FULL 25RT, B1, or A2 will result in a calculation that only includes the full length 
runway, intersection B1, or intersection A2 respectively.   
If there are more than 3 intersections, the ALL button will change to FIRST 4 and selecting 
that button will result in 4 results; a calculation that includes the full length runway and the 
first 3 intersections. 
If your administrator has excluded the ALL selection, ALL will not be shown as an 
available selection and only individual calculations are available.  
 
Selecting Runway Condition 
Clicking on the CONDITION button will display the list of runway conditions that your 
administrator has set up.  A typical selection might look like this: 
 
In this example, the possible choices are for dry, wet, standing water, slush, and slippery 
runway conditions of good, medium, and poor.  If the user selects STANDING WATER

Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 161 
or SLUSH, OPT will then display a window to ask either how deep is the standing water 
or slush.  Once the selections and responses have been made, the button’s label will display 
the results in green as in the example below. 
 
Entering Wind 
Wind inputs may be made in either wind component or direction and magnitude  into the 
WIND edit box.  Depending on how your installation of OPT  is set up, you may also see 
the head/tail and crosswind components displayed under the wind input box as shown 
below.  If the wind is input in wind component, headwinds are considered to be positive 
and tailwinds negative.  The correct format for wind in the direction/magnitude format is 
just that, direction/magnitude, e.g. 040/20 would be a 20 knot wind coming from a 
magnetic heading of 40 degrees.  The wind component is then resolved by comparing this 
information with the runway heading.  After the cursor has left t he input box, units are 
appended to the user’s input to show how OPT has interpreted the input.  If only inputting 
the headwind or tailwind, one may change the input units by adding, for instance, an “M” 
to the input component, such as -5M.  This would then be interpreted as a 5 m/s tailwind.  
An input of 5K would be interpreted as a 5 kt headwind.  Additionally, a headwind or 
tailwind may be denoted in the entry by appending an “H” or a “T” to the wind magnitude, 
such as 5T for a 5 kt tailwind. 
 
Entering OAT 
OAT is entered into the OAT edit box.  Again, depending on your installation, the alternate 
unit (C or F) may be shown under your input.  If the user desires to input temperature in 
units not expected by OPT, simply place a ‘C’ or ‘F’ after the temperature (e.g. 59F) and 
OPT will make the correct conversion.   Similar to the wind input, after the cursor leaves 
the edit box, the units that are assumed are displayed in the edit box as shown below  and 
the alternate units are shown below the edit box. 
 
 Entering QNH 
QNH, or pressure variation, may also be input in two different units, namely HPa (mb), or 
inches of Mercury (Hg).  OPT  will check the magnitude of this input and convert 
accordingly.  Any inputs greater than 100 will be interpreted as HPa, while anything less 
will be interpreted as inches Hg.  Depending on your installation, the converted values may 
be displayed under your input. 


   
  OPT Administrator’s Guide 
  
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See page ii for details. 
Page 162 
 
Airplane Configuration Inputs 
Once the airport, runway, and atmospheric inputs are made, the crew may specify the 
required airplane configuration inputs .  When there are selectable derates available, the 
OPT user interface (UI) will include a rating dropdown button.  If it is allowed by the 
administrator, this list may also include Optimum  and Windshear selections.  Thes e 
selections will compute the best combination of fixed derate plus assumed temperature for 
maximum derate or special windshear guidance information respectively.   
Other common airplane configuration and policy inputs are made through several other 
available dropdown buttons.    Depending on your airplane type, these buttons might 
include:  
• Flaps 
• Air conditioning 
• Anti-ice 
• APU 
• V1 policy 
• Improved climb policy 
• Reverse thrust availability 
• Alternate forward c.g. limit 
If allowed by the administrator, the flap s election pull down menu may include an 
Optimum selection.  If this option is chosen, the software will find the optimum takeoff 
flap position between the highest and lowest setting available in the allowable list set up 
by the administrator.  If optimum is  the only setting allowed, the Onboard Performance 
Tool will choose between all of the certified flap positions for that airplane.  In some cases, 
when a departure procedure is selected that is valid for only a specific flap(s), the flap 
selection list will only contain that flap position(s).  
If selected by the administrator, the flap selection pull down menu may include a 
Preferred selection.  If this option is chosen, the software will attempt to use a single, 
preferred flap position specified by the adm inistrator.  If the performance available is not 
sufficient, OPT will revert to using Optimum flaps for its calculation. 
Miscellaneous Inputs 
Other inputs may be available on your installation of OPT.  These might consist of: 
• Flight Number - The flight number may be manually recorded in this input box.  
This box initially contains a default value set up by the administrator. 


 
OPT Administrator’s Guide   
 
Boeing Proprietary     Copyright © Boeing.    May be subject to export restrictions under EAR. See title page for details. 
Page 163 
• Crew - Crew identification information can be entered here.  This data is stored in 
the electronic file that is updated when data is calculated as noted above. 
Takeoff Weight and CG 
In Takeoff Weight edit box, the crew should enter the actual, or planned weight for the 
flight.  The weight may be entered in either ones or thousands (102500 or 102.5).  After 
this is done, and the Calculate button becomes active and is clicked, the Onboard 
Performance Tool  will then calculate both max thrust and assumed temperature 
information based on this weight.  If the weight that is input exceeds the performance 
limited maximum takeoff weight,  the Onboa rd Performance Tool  will display an error 
message during the calculation process to alert the user and display the maximum weight.  
When returning from the Weight & Balance screen, if the Complete button was used, this 
field will be automatically populated with the takeoff weight from that page. 
If available, once the takeoff weight has been input, the CG  edit box becomes active and 
is available for input.  This input is used only for the calculation of stab trim or Complex 
Crosswind limits  (if used) and does not affect  takeoff performance.  Like the Takeoff 
Weight input, this field will automatically be populated when returning from the Weight 
and Balance screen using the Complete button. 
Assumed Temp 
The ATM edit box also becomes active when a value is entered into the Takeoff Weight 
box.  For this input, any number entered that is less than or equal to zero will be treated as 
a decrement from the maximum possible assumed temperature that the Onboard 
Performance Tool calculates.  For a maximum assumed temperature calculation the user 
may input either a zero or “MAX”.  Any number greater than zero will be considered to be 
a user desired assumed temperature.  If the user -input temperature is greater than the 
maximum allowable, an error message will be displayed to alert the user.  The user should 
then either input a new assumed temperature or let the Onboard Performance Tool calculate 
the maximum assumed temperature as described above.
